VChalking Nick in Nelson
p207
sg5
Vhttp://blog.greens.org.nz/2009/10/27/chalking-nick-in-nelson/
p208
sg7
(lp209
sg9
V<p>Chalking the opinion of many on the streets of Nelson this morning...</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://blog.greens.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/No-Mining.JPG"><img class="aligncenter size-medium wp-image-7227" title="No Mining" src="http://blog.greens.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/No-Mining-300x225.jpg" alt="No Mining" width="300" height="225" /></a></p>\u000A<p>A National Government created Schedule 4 of the Crown Minerals Act in 1997 to protect National Parks from mining.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://blog.greens.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/P1010022.JPG"><img class="aligncenter size-medium wp-image-7228" title="P1010022" src="http://blog.greens.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/P1010022-300x110.jpg" alt="P1010022" width="300" height="110" /></a></p>\u000A<p>The Government wants to mine in Kahurangi National Park, a Park created by National while Nick Smith was Conservation Minister and proudly opened in 1996 by Jim Bolger.</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://blog.greens.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/Get-active.JPG"><img class="aligncenter size-medium wp-image-7229" title="Get active" src="http://blog.greens.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/Get-active-300x225.jpg" alt="Get active" width="300" height="225" /></a></p>\u000A<p>So, why does Nick Smith support this move?</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://blog.greens.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/diggers-out.JPG"><img class="aligncenter size-medium wp-image-7230" title="diggers out" src="http://blog.greens.org.nz/wp-content/uploads/diggers-out-300x103.jpg" alt="diggers out" width="300" height="103" /></a></p>\u000A<p>Here is Nick's 1997 speech [not online] when the Schedule was created:</p>\u000A<blockquote>\u000A<p>Thursday, November 20, 1997</p>\u000A<p>Hon. NICK SMITH (Minister of Conservation): In rising to support the third reading of the Bill, I draw the House's attention to the significance of the final stages of the passage of this legislation. ...</p>\u000A<p>This Bill at long last puts some pegs in the sand in some very significant areas of New Zealand and says to the mining industries of New Zealand: "These are no-go areas."</p>\u000A<p>I draw the House's attention this afternoon to just how significant that range of areas is. First, we have all those areas that are national parks: areas such as the Abel Tasman National Park, and the national parks of Arthur's Pass, Egmont, Fiordland, Kahurangi, Mount Aspiring, Mount Cook, Nelson Lakes, Paparoa, Tongariro, Te Urewera, Westland, and Whanganui. Those areas total over 3 million hectares of land. This legislation says to the mining industries that those areas set aside as national parks are not appropriate areas for mining.</p>\u000A<p>If one picks up the National Parks Act and sees the quite prohibitive range of activities that is permitted to go on in those areas, one realises that it is certainly consistent with those activities to say that<strong> mining should not occur in those areas</strong>. In effect, this legislation we are about to pass sets and strengthens that National Parks Act, which dates back to 1980.</p>\u000A<p>This legislation goes further than just national parks. Areas around New Zealand have been set aside as nature reserves, scientific reserves, wilderness areas, sanctuaries, and wildlife sanctuaries. There are areas that have been set aside as Ramsar sites, in terms of the convention on wetlands and highly migratory birds, as well as those areas in the Coromandel that the Alliance member Jeanette Fitzsimons has mentioned. This Bill sets out quite clearly very significant areas of conservation estate in which mining is not allowed. That is something that this House should welcome.</p>\u000A<p>In 1990 National's manifesto committed it to going down this route. .... the commitment that was made in 1990 to ban mining in national parks was a significant one. ... the Bill does provide a mechanism, which has been improved in the Committee stage, whereby additional areas can be added to those that will be provided for in the mining ban.</p>\u000A<p>I also wish to make comment about my New Zealand First colleagues and their attitude to this Bill. Members will note that the coalition agreement specifically mentions the banning of mining in national parks. Again, I would draw to the attention of this House that the Government is honouring a further clause of the coalition agreement by advancing this legislation.</p>\u000A<p>Environmental groups-the Royal Forest and Bird Protection Society, the Maruia Society, and groups in the Coromandel-have pushed for this legislation for a very long time. I welcome its progress. I want to make reference to the cooperative way in which members on both sides of the House have worked to progress this legislation. ....</p>\u000A<p>This is landmark legislation for the conservation movement in New Zealand. I welcome the Bill's progress and, as Minister of Conservation, look forward to not having to consider mining applications in those areas where nature should be able to rule the roost.</p>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A<p>What's changed, Nick?</p>\u000A<div id="_mcePaste">Mining<!-- v:* { 	BEHAVIOR: url(#default#VML) } o:* { 	BEHAVIOR: url(#default#VML) } w:* { 	BEHAVIOR: url(#default#VML) } .shape { 	BEHAVIOR: url(#default#VML) } --><!-- st1:* { 	BEHAVIOR: url(#default#ieooui) } --><!-- @font-face { 	font-family: PMingLiU; } @font-face { 	font-family: Tahoma; } @font-face { 	font-family: @PMingLiU; } @page Section1 {size: 595.3pt 841.9pt; margin: 72.0pt 90.0pt 72.0pt 90.0pt; } P.MsoNormal { 	FONT-SIZE: 12pt; MARGIN: 0cm 0cm 0pt; FONT-FAMILY: "Times New Roman" } LI.MsoNormal { 	FONT-SIZE: 12pt; MARGIN: 0cm 0cm 0pt; FONT-FAMILY: "Times New Roman" } DIV.MsoNormal { 	FONT-SIZE: 12pt; MARGIN: 0cm 0cm 0pt; FONT-FAMILY: "Times New Roman" } A:link { 	COLOR: blue; TEXT-DECORATION: underline } SPAN.MsoHyperlink { 	COLOR: blue; TEXT-DECORATION: underline } A:visited { 	COLOR: blue; TEXT-DECORATION: underline } SPAN.MsoHyperlinkFollowed { 	COLOR: blue; TEXT-DECORATION: underline } P { 	FONT-SIZE: 12pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0cm; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0cm; FONT-FAMILY: "Times New Roman"; mso-margin-top-alt: auto; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto } SPAN.EmailStyle18 { 	COLOR: navy; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; mso-style-type: personal-reply } DIV.Section1 { 	page: Section1 } --></p>\u000A<div dir="ltr"><span class="458555603-05102009"><span>Thursday,  November 20, 1997<br />\u000A</span></span><span class="458555603-05102009"><span>Hon. NICK SMITH (Minister of  Conservation): In rising to support the third reading of the Bill, I draw the  House's attention to the significance of the final stages of the passage of this  legislation. The role of mining in New Zealand has been a controversial  issue right from the last century, when mining was given preferred status as a  land use. In fact, if we look at the history in the West Coast, Otago, or Nelson  regions, we see that miners were put on a pedestal. Rights of access to land  would be given to them over and above rights being given to other persons. </span></span></div>\u000A<div dir="ltr">\u000A<p class="MsoNormal"><span>Over  the last decade we have seen a number of pieces of significant legislation that  effectively bring mining activities into line with other land uses, be they  tourism, farming, or other sorts of land use. In 1991 we saw the passage of the  Crown Minerals Act. That was landmark legislation, in that it stated at long  last that miners could not walk on to private property and trample all over  those private property owners' rights. They had to get the consent of the  landowners. </span></p>\u000A<p class="MsoNormal"><span>However, at that time the  issue of conservation land, which makes up about one-third of the land of New Zealand, was left in abeyance. This  Bill at long last puts some pegs in the sand in some very significant areas of  New Zealand and says to the mining industries of New Zealand: "These are no-go  areas." </span></p>\u000A<p class="MsoNormal"><span>I draw  the House's attention this afternoon to just how significant that range of areas  is. First, we have all those areas that are national parks: areas such as the  Abel Tasman National  Park, and the national parks of Arthur's Pass, Egmont,  Fiordland, Kahurangi, Mount  Aspiring, Mount Cook, Nelson Lakes,  Paparoa, Tongariro, Te Urewera, Westland, and Whanganui. Those areas total over  3 million hectares of land. This legislation says to the mining industries that  those areas set aside as national parks are not appropriate areas for mining. </span></p>\u000A<p class="MsoNormal"><span>If one  picks up the National Parks Act and sees the quite prohibitive range of  activities that is permitted to go on in those areas, one realises that it is  certainly consistent with those activities to say that mining should not occur  in those areas. In effect, this legislation we are about to pass sets and  strengthens that National Parks Act, which dates back to 1980. </span></p>\u000A<p class="MsoNormal"><span>This  legislation goes further than just national parks. Areas around  New  Zealand have been set aside as nature reserves,  scientific reserves, wilderness areas, sanctuaries, and wildlife sanctuaries.  There are areas that have been set aside as Ramsar sites, in terms of the  convention on wetlands and highly migratory birds, as well as those areas in the  Coromandel that the Alliance member Jeanette Fitzsimons has  mentioned. This Bill sets out quite clearly very significant areas of  conservation estate in which mining is not allowed. That is something that this  House should welcome. </span></p>\u000A<p class="MsoNormal"><span>In  1990 National's manifesto committed it to going down this route. I accept it has  been- </span></p>\u000A<p class="MsoNormal"><span>Judith  Tizard: What about the surcharge? </span></p>\u000A<p class="MsoNormal"><span>Hon.  NICK SMITH: Yes, and I have to say that the commitment that was made in 1990 to  ban mining in national parks was a significant one. While the member Judith  Tizard may chuckle away, I have to say that in 6 years of Labour Administration  no move was made on this issue. That is partly, as I am sure she will  acknowledge, because there are substantial interests that the member for the  West Coast would have about ecological areas. It has been a highly contentious  issue in the select committee as to which areas and classifications of land  would be included in this mining ban and which would not. What is more, the Bill  does provide a mechanism, which has been improved in the Committee stage,  whereby additional areas can be added to those that will be provided for in the  mining ban. </span></p>\u000A<p class="MsoNormal"><span>I also  wish to make comment about my New Zealand First colleagues and their attitude to  this Bill. Members will note that the coalition agreement specifically mentions  the banning of mining in national parks. Again, I would draw to the attention of  this House that the Government is honouring a further clause of the coalition  agreement by advancing this legislation. </span></p>\u000A<p class="MsoNormal"><span>Environmental groups-the  Royal  Forest and Bird Protection  Society, the Maruia Society, and groups in the Coromandel-have pushed for this  legislation for a very long time. I welcome its progress. I want to make  reference to the cooperative way in which members on both sides of the House  have worked to progress this legislation. I specifically want to mention  Christine Fletcher, from National, who has had particular passions about the  area of Coromandel, as has the Labour member Judith Tizard. I also want to  mention the previous Minister of Energy, Doug Kidd, who was very much involved  in the brokering of this legislation and in finding the way through the  different areas, and in deciding how they might be treated. </span></p>\u000A<p class="MsoNormal"><span>This  is landmark legislation for the conservation movement in New Zealand. I  welcome the Bill's progress and, as Minister of Conservation, look forward to  not having to consider mining applications in those areas where nature should be  able to rule the roost. </span></p>\u000A</div>\u000A</div>

VMSD social report 2009: Inequality increased in Labour's last year in office
p214
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/typepad/liberationbybryceedwards/~3/pV2avRiI8d4/msd-social-report-2009-inequality-increased-in-labours-last-year-in-office.html
p215
sg7
(lp216
sg9
VThe Ministry of Social Development has silently released its annual Social Report for 2009 \u2013 no doubt attempting to keep the findings under the radar. Likewise, the National Government has refrained from releasing a single press release on it (as yet). As always with the wealth of statistics in such reports, there is the good and the bad to be seized upon, and these things can be spun by the left and the right, and the various partisans in many different ways. I\u2019ll leave Labour and National to give the positive spin on the current stats \u2013 and much of the negative material reflects poorly on the past Labour Government, for which the period of this report effectively covers. Instead, this blog post highlight some of the negative material that immediately sticks out from a browse of the report. There is one particular domain within the report that shows serious problems: \u2018Economic Standard of Living\u2019. Basically, since the last annual report \u2013 and thus during Labour\u2019s last year in office \u2013 New Zealand became a less equal society, with increased inequality and greater poverty. [Read more below]

VGiving the finger to the labour movement
p223
sg5
Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2009/10/giving-finger-to-labour-movement.html
p224
sg7
(lp225
sg9
V<p>So, the day after <a href="http://www.labourday.org.nz/">Labour Day</a>, the government introduces legislation to <a href="http://www.scoop.co.nz/stories/PA0910/S00393.htm">steal your meal and rest breaks</a>.  Talk about giving the finger to the labour movement.\u000A\u000A<p>The <a href="http://www.legislation.govt.nz/bill/government/2009/0091/latest/whole.html#dlm2440327">bill</a> will replace the <a href="http://www.legislation.govt.nz/act/public/2000/0024/latest/DLM1940671.html#DLM1940671">existing statutory rights to meal and rest breaks</a> with a vague requirement for "reasonable" and "appropriate" breaks which may in fact require the employee to continue working, are taken at the time specified by the employer, and which may not in fact be provided <i>at all</i> if "compensatory measures" (such as a later start time, an earlier finish time or accumulated time off) are provided.  Given that the length of the work day is purely nominal and that such time off may be unpaid, the result is to remove the right entirely.\u000A\u000A<p>And that's National's approach to employment relations in a nutshell: turning enforceable rights into grace and favour which we must beg for, like a peasant to a lord.  And while it will make no difference in most workplaces, the workplaces where it <i>is</i> necessary - where employees are denied the basic dignities of not feeling hungry or thirsty or not having to piss themselves while working - will have just got themselves an abuser's charter.  By changing the law, national is explicitly supporting these abusive employers.\u000A\u000A<p>The bill was, according to the explanatory note, "developed at speed and without significant consultation".  And it will be passed under urgency.  The Regulatory Impact Statement (such as it is - this is another bill which bypassed the normal requirements) notes that it is expected to become law by the end of the year, meaning no real time for select committee consideration.  That is assuming they don't ram it through without a select committee stage at all to get it in by 1 November to avoid having to negotiate properly with regional air traffic controllers.  But that just seems to be the way this government operates: legislate in haste, and leave us to repent at leisure.<div class="blogger-post-footer"><img width="1" height="1" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/tracker/5054264-8630127152829255619?l=norightturn.blogspot.com" /></div>

VClimate change: $225,000 per job?
p232
sg5
Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2009/10/climate-change-225000-per-job.html
p233
sg7
(lp234
sg9
V<p><i>Carbon News</i> this morning reports that the government's pollution subsidies to the Tiwai Point Aluminium smelter sum to an enormous $209 million - or <a href="http://www.scoop.co.nz/stories/PO0910/S00381.htm">$225,000 per job</a> (more than an MP's slary) for each of the 930 workers the smelter employs.  It's a massive indictment of the subsidy scheme.  Or is it?\u000A\u000A<p>Delving into the figures, it seems they are based on not just the direct subsidy to Rio Tinto, but also the opportunity cost of their exclusive use of the power from Manapouri - power that could instead be used elsewhere, allowing the dirty inefficient coal-fired Huntly Power Station to be closed down.  And unfortunately, the latter massively outweighs the former:\u000A<blockquote>\u000A<i>Replacing the emissions-intensive Huntly with Manapouri would result in a net decrease in liabilities to taxpay¬ers of $209 million per annum, made up of the non-payment of the Rio Tinto subsidy ($14 million) and the non-payment of the Huntly subsidy ($195 million),\u201D he said.</i>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A\u000AThis is I think an unfair loading of costs when we're talking about a per-job subsidy.  Besides, its not as if $15,000 per job in direct subsidies for Tiwai Point's emissions is anything to be sneezed at. So on that front I think <i>Carbon News</i> massively overstates the case.  But they have made a very good argument for shutting down Tiwai Point entirely.  After all, Rio Tinto's own figures show a maximum annual benefit to New Zealand of <a href="http://norightturn.blogspot.com/2008/05/climate-change-hoisting-rio-tinto-with.html">$121.2 million per year</a>.  With current carbon costs of $209 million per year - and it <i>is</i> fair to count the opportunity cost of running Huntly when we're looking at an overall cost-benefit analysis - we're looking at being at least $88 million a year better off if we close the place down, which increases to $100 million once you remove the "benefit" of deferred grid upgrades (which we are already paying).  This rises to over $300 million a year post-2012 when carbon prices are expected to be higher and Tiwai Point's output lower.\u000A\u000A<p>What this shows us is that Rio Tinto are just leeches.  Once the environmental costs are counted, their presence makes us actively worse-off as a society, and significantly so.  We should not be paying these people pollution subsidies; instead we should be shutting them down.  And the sooner that happens, the better off we will be.<div class="blogger-post-footer"><img width="1" height="1" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/tracker/5054264-1594234172642257780?l=norightturn.blogspot.com" /></div>

VMMP means representation
p239

Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2009/10/mmp-means-representation.html

(lp241

V<p>One new addition to the <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/">Social Report</a> this year is a section on <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/civil-political-rights/representation-ethnic-groups-government.html">representation of ethnic groups in government</a>.  The graph speaks for itself about what MMP has meant for ethnic representation:\u000A\u000A<p><b>Members of Parliament identifying as M\u0101ori, Pacific peoples or Asian 1984\u20132008, and M\u0101ori, Pacific peoples or Asian share of the total population</b><br />\u000A<img src="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/images/sr/cp3-1.gif" />\u000A\u000A<p>The bars are percentages of MPs, the dots (taken from census data) are percentages of the population.  So, we have a way to go yet, but MMP has still resulted in a massive improvement and given us a Parliament that looks a lot more like New Zealand.  That will likely disappear if the electoral system is changed - a tremendous loss to the legitimacy of our political system, and to New Zealand.<div class="blogger-post-footer"><img width="1" height="1" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/tracker/5054264-3060198936613714148?l=norightturn.blogspot.com" /></div>

VSocial Report 2009
p246
sg5
Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2009/10/social-report-2009.html
p247
sg7
(lp248
sg9
V<p>The <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/">2009 Social Report</a> has finally been released. Normally it would have come out by August, but this year was unaccountably delayed, Cabinet not signing off on it until last week.  I guess they just didn't view it as a priority.  Unfortunately, it has also fallen victim to some extent to the government's drive to cut costs, so instead of it being published as a hardcopy (and available for future researchers in libraries), it is now a web-only publication.  Which is so much more fragile.  Important government data like this should not be published only in a digital medium.  \u000A\u000A<p>Most of the data in this report dates from 2006-2008, so its Labour's legacy that is being reported on: lower (though now rising again) <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/economic-standard-living/income-inequality.html">income inequality</a>, increased <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/paid-work/median-hourly-earnings.html">median hourly earnings</a>, and the stubborn persistence of ethnic gaps in <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/health/life-expectancy.html">life expectancy</a>.  It also shows the consequences of their education policies, with decreased <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/knowledge-skills/participation-tertiary-education.html">participation in tertiary education</a> (particularly among M\u0101ori and Pacific Peoples) thanks to their racist stomping on the w\u0101nanga.  Meanwhile, <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/economic-standard-living/housing-affordability.html">housing unaffordability</a> is at an all time high, with a flow-on effect on <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/economic-standard-living/population-low-incomes.html">child poverty</a> which has unravelled all the good work done by Working For Families.  But you won't read any of this in the <a href="http://www.msd.govt.nz/documents/about-msd-and-our-work/newsroom/media-releases/news/2009/social-report-fact-sheet-2009.doc">key findings</a>: their focus is relentlessly long-term, concentrating on improvements since the 80's and 90's rather than recent (and politically attributable) changes.\u000A\u000A<p>Next year's report - if it happens - will begin to show the effects of National's policies.  Unfortunately, the 2009 data in this one on <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/paid-work/unemployment.html">unemployment</a>, <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/paid-work/employment.html">employment participation</a> and <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/economic-standard-living/market-income-person.html">incomes</a> is not good.  In their first year, the standard of living of the average New Zealander has dropped.  While they're not responsible for the recession, they are responsible for dealing with it and reducing the impact on New Zealanders - and by these statistics, their reaction has so far been a failure.\u000A\u000A<p>You can download the full report <a href="http://socialreport.msd.govt.nz/documents/social-report-2009.pdf">here</a> [PDF].<div class="blogger-post-footer"><img width="1" height="1" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/tracker/5054264-2842001416150800852?l=norightturn.blogspot.com" /></div>

VThe consequences of double-bunking
p253
sg5
Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2009/10/consequences-of-double-bunking.html
p254
sg7
(lp255
sg9
V<p>When the government first floated plans to use <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10580279">double bunking</a> to overcrowd prisons, criminologists warned that it would lead to <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10560955">rapes, bullying and violence</a>.  And now we can add <a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/the-press/news/christchurch/2987910/Fear-of-attacker-prompted-prison-suicide-sources">suicide</a> to that list:\u000A<blockquote>\u000A<i>A prisoner, who had been raped by another inmate, killed himself after learning his attacker was being brought back to the same prison, prison sources say.\u000A\u000A<p>The Corrections Department says an independent review into Michael Graham Maxwell's death means it cannot comment.\u000A\u000A<p>[...]\u000A\u000A<p>Maxwell's funeral was held on Tuesday in Hoon Hay.\u000A\u000A<p>He died in Christchurch Hospital on Friday after being found in his Christchurch Men's Prison cell on October 10.\u000A\u000A<p>Maxwell was repeatedly raped in Christchurch Men's Prison in 2005, after being placed in the same cell as Noble, a violent gang member.\u000A\u000A<p>A prison source said Maxwell, 24, committed suicide after other inmates taunted him that Noble was being brought back to the prison.</i>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A\u000AThere's more in today's papers about how Maxwell had <a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10605586">sought help</a> - including ACC counselling - for psychological issues caused by his rape, and how he had <a href="http://www.stuff.co.nz/national/3000699/Man-raped-in-prison-pleaded-with-PM-for-help">pleaded with the Prime Minister</a> to be allowed into a proper rehabilitation programme.  Those pleas were ignored.  As a result, a man is dead.\u000A\u000A<p>No doubt the Sensible Sentencing Trust will soon issue a press release saying "good riddance", but there are two points we should remember.  Firstly, the protection of the law extends to everyone, even to convicted criminals; that is what differentiates the state from a gang.  There has been a clear failure in their duty of car eon the part of Corrections which has led directly to a man's death, and they need to be held accountable for it.  Secondly, despite the Sensible Sentencing Trust's <a href="http://norightturn.blogspot.com/2009/09/dropping-mask.html">urgent fantasies</a>, we do not have the death penalty in New Zealand.  At least, not in law.  But double bunking will give us one <i>de facto</i>.  And that is simply unacceptable in a civilised society.<div class="blogger-post-footer"><img width="1" height="1" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/tracker/5054264-2537208692853821383?l=norightturn.blogspot.com" /></div>

VWe're paying for Rodney's fundraising trip
p260
sg5
Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2009/10/were-paying-for-rodneys-fundraising.html
p261
sg7
(lp262
sg9
V<p>Last week we learned that Local Government Minister Rodney Hide was <a href="http://norightturn.blogspot.com/2009/10/perk-of-office.html">treating his job as a corrupt little fiefdom</a>, giving speeches within his portfolio and charging stakeholders a donation to the ACT party if they wanted to hear them in <a href="http://www.cabinetmanual.cabinetoffice.govt.nz/2.50#2.52">clear contravention of Ministerial guidelines</a>.  That's bad enough, but the response to an urgent OIA request has added insult to injury - we're paying for his travel as well:\u000A<blockquote>\u000A<i>On Wednesday 4 November, Mr Hide will be in Christchurch on business related to his Ministerial portfolios of Local Government and Regulatory Reform. The purpose of this trip is to deliver a keynote address to the Canterbury Manufacturers Association on the principles behind his Regulatory Reform programme. While he is in Christchurch he will also be making site visits to a local engineering firm and the University of Canterbury. Mr Hide will also be meeting with members of the press and conducting other Ministerial duties.\u000A\u000A<p>There will be no additional costs to Vote: Ministerial Services related to Mr Hide's address to the ACT Party at the Heartland Cotswald Hotel.</i>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A\u000ASure, there's no additional costs to the taxpayer, and it is of course all within the rules, but it is an unacceptable mingling of public and private business.  Thanks to some clever scheduling, we're effectively footing the bill for Hide's attendance at his little fundraiser.  And we simply shouldn't be.  The Ministerial travel budget is to pay for travel as part of Ministerial duties - not for Ministers to zip around the country touching up donors for cash.\u000A\u000A<p>More generally, Ministers need to be able to maintain a rigid separation between their public duties and their private business.  But like some feudal lord, Hide seems unable to tell the difference.  If he cannot distinguish between the two, then he is simply unfit to be a Minister.<div class="blogger-post-footer"><img width="1" height="1" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/tracker/5054264-64111663657934582?l=norightturn.blogspot.com" /></div>

VGuest column: Labour Day
p267
sg5
Vhttp://norightturn.blogspot.com/2009/10/guest-column-labour-day.html
p268
sg7
(lp269
sg9
V<p>By <a href="http://www.labourday.org.nz/">Stephen Day</a>\u000A\u000A<p>I've always thought that there is something counterintuitive about unionists organising activity around Labour Day. Labour Day has come to mean, for most New Zealanders, a day off because, well, we deserve to have a day off. It's nice to have a place in our year dedicated to not needing to do anything, just taking a break.\u000A\u000A<p>Sure, during our early Labour Days we had big festivals, parades and sporting occasions. But these days Labour Day can quite happily be about little more than sleeping in, hopefully sitting about in the sun and maybe spending more time than you might usually with friends or family.\u000A\u000A<p>This year hasn't been the best one for workers and union members. Most employers, including the biggest employer of them all, the one we elect, have responded to the global recession by zipping up their wallet and bunkering down. It's tough times for employers as well as workers. On the whole workers, through their unions, have tried to work cooperatively with their employers within these new financial constraints. However some employers, who haven't faced tough times, who are in fact continuing to make large profits, are exploiting the situation to batter their workers and generate more profits. Many workers are still after all theses years still not getting paid enough to look after a family and live a decent life.  Many face working conditions that are unnecessarily harsh, lacking in respect or dignity, or even downright dangerous. \u000A\u000A<p>But despite all that there are still things to celebrate.  We now have paid parental leave.  We have legislated meal breaks, breastfeeding breaks, four weeks annual leave and regular increases to the minimum wage.  We achieved all these things in the recent past.  We achieved all theses things by working together and campaigning for them.\u000A\u000A<p>Not everyone will get a holiday on Monday but most will, and another recent victory by working people and our unions means that those who don't still get a day in lieu.\u000A\u000A<p>My advice is don't spend Monday thinking about unions and working conditions.  It's a holiday so enjoy it doing stuff you want to do.  But the next day, Tuesday, go to say hello to the union delegate at your worksite and ask if there is anything simple you can do to help to win the next small improvement for workers and our families.<div class="blogger-post-footer"><img width="1" height="1" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/tracker/5054264-5923767424441813926?l=norightturn.blogspot.com" /></div>

VMyopic electrification works
p306
sg5
Vhttp://tumeke.blogspot.com/2009/10/myopic-electrification-works_27.html
p307
sg7
(lp308
sg9
V<a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_Yu6lJst3lkM/SuYxagRgldI/AAAAAAAAFhM/MCGNt0ViIJA/s1600-h/7km_tunnel.jpg"><img src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_Yu6lJst3lkM/SuYxagRgldI/AAAAAAAAFhM/MCGNt0ViIJA/s400/7km_tunnel.jpg" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5397055534859851218" /></a><br /><a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=10605540&ref=rss">NZ Herald</a> reporting:<a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_Yu6lJst3lkM/SuYlNkmjRQI/AAAAAAAAFhE/k45_2O_mceU/s1600-h/Picture+2.png"><img src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_Yu6lJst3lkM/SuYlNkmjRQI/AAAAAAAAFhE/k45_2O_mceU/s400/Picture+2.png" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5397042118544016642" /></a><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_Yu6lJst3lkM/SuYyOqAeQpI/AAAAAAAAFhU/6VRBvNXLPOY/s1600-h/mainline2-jpg-071-240x180.jpg"><img src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_Yu6lJst3lkM/SuYyOqAeQpI/AAAAAAAAFhU/6VRBvNXLPOY/s200/mainline2-jpg-071-240x180.jpg" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5397056430825947794" /></a>They - the authorities, the rail company - closed the Parnell station. Demolished it I believe. But the article doesn't mention that history at all - and since I can't find any references on the internet I guess it's just an unproven assertion on my part, but I'm sure there was a small station building and platform just down from the depot that they are talking about.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.aucklandtrains.co.nz/2009/10/20/plan-for-historic-parnell-train-station-gathers-steam/">Pictures</a> of Parnell site. <br /><br /><a href="http://www.aucklandtrains.co.nz/2009/10/24/next-step-along-long-track-to-electrification/">Auckland Trains blog</a> has some photos of the electrification preparation. Not that I think it will be delivered as long as the structure and funding is deliberately hamstrung by Wellington, but works are clearly underway.<a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_Yu6lJst3lkM/SuY0mPoUcVI/AAAAAAAAFhc/ObM3ta96mLY/s1600-h/Picture+7.png"><img src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_Yu6lJst3lkM/SuY0mPoUcVI/AAAAAAAAFhc/ObM3ta96mLY/s400/Picture+7.png" border="0" alt="" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5397059035085435218" /></a>And this is where Auckland puts on the dunce cap once again. It's all in aid of an over-head system. <br /><br />Why? Why does the electrification have to be over-head? Why do ugly over-head wires and gantries etc. have to be erected?<br /><br />Because no-one has contemplated the alternative of a third rail/track electrification system? No rolling stock has been purchased - there's never been any real funding commitment - and yet the presumption is it should be above ground and not at ground level. Why? <br /><br />Because of the level crossings? Because they are too slack to fence off the lines? We have an opportunity to do it right, but just watch them do it all wrong - and spends untold millions in the process. The one advantage Auckland does have - that things aren't set in concrete and are undeveloped will be pissed away. Just watch.<br /><br />In the year 2099 when electrification does arrive it will be accompanied by an unnecessary  mess of wires above the tracks - that's where this is going. If the reason for going over-head is because it's faster and cheaper we should realise that it never pans out that way. Same thing with the horrible cane plantation-type narrow gauge - we'll stick with that even if it turns out we could have replaced a majority of that through the current upgrade process anyway. Hopeless.<div class="blogger-post-footer"><img width="1" height="1" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/tracker/12465152-1559994140693709083?l=tumeke.blogspot.com" /></div>

VObama and the Nobel Prize: When War becomes Peace, When the Lie becomes the Truth
p341
sg5
Vhttp://uncensored.co.nz/2009/10/27/obama-and-the-nobel-prize-when-war-becomes-peace-when-the-lie-becomes-the-truth/

(lp343

V<p>by  Michel  Chossudovsky</p>\u000A<p>From <a href="http://www.globalresearch.ca/index.php?context=va&aid=15622">Globalresearch</a></p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify"><em>[ ... almost threw up in my own mouth when I heard Obama had been given the peace prize. </em></p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify"><em>All that smooth-talking mannequin has done so far is emulate the planet fisting policies of his ape-minded predecessor, Bush II ] </em></p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify"><img src="http://www.pressenza.com/uploads/assets/2009-08-15-00073.1280x960.jpg" alt="http://www.pressenza.com/uploads/assets/2009-08-15-00073.1280x960.jpg" width="680" height="395" /></p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify"><em><br />\u000A</em></p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">When war becomes peace,</p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">When concepts and realities are turned upside down,</p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">When fiction becomes truth and truth becomes fiction.</p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">When a global military agenda is heralded as a humanitarian endeavor,</p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">When the killing of civilians is upheld as "collateral damage",</p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">When those who resist the US-NATO led invasion of their homeland are categorized as "insurgents" or "terrorists".</p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">When preemptive nuclear war is upheld as self defense.</p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">When advanced torture and "interrogation" techniques are routinely used to "protect peacekeeping operations",</p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">When tactical nuclear weapons are heralded by the Pentagon as "harmless to the surrounding civilian population"</p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">When three quarters of US personal federal income tax revenues are allocated to financing what is euphemistically referred to as "national defense"</p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">When the Commander in Chief of the largest military force on planet earth is presented as a global peace-maker,</p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify">When the Lie becomes the Truth.</p>\u000A<p dir="ltr" align="justify"><img src="http://juliannahaz.files.wordpress.com/2009/06/us_army_afghanistan_2006.jpg" alt="http://juliannahaz.files.wordpress.com/2009/06/us_army_afghanistan_2006.jpg" width="682" height="446" /></p>\u000A<p align="justify"><span><strong>Obama's "War Without Borders"</strong></span></p>\u000A<p>We are the crossroads of the most serious crisis in modern history. The US in partnership with NATO and Israel has launched a global military adventure which, in a very real sense, threatens the future of humanity.</p>\u000A<p align="justify">At this critical juncture in our history, the Norwegian Nobel Committee's decision to award the Nobel Peace Prize to President and Commander in Chief Barack Obama constitutes an unmitigated tool of propaganda and distortion, which unreservedly supports the Pentagon's "Long War":  "A War without Borders" in the true sense of the word, characterised by the Worlwide deployment of US military might.</p>\u000A<p align="justify">Apart from the diplomatic rhetoric, there has been no meaningful reversal of US foreign policy in relation to the George W. Bush presidency, which might have remotely justified the granting of the Nobel Prize to Obama. In fact quite the opposite. The Obama military agenda has sought to extend the war into new frontiers. With a new team of military and foreign policy advisers, the Obama war agenda has been far more effective in fostering military escalation than that formulated by the NeoCons.</p>\u000A<p align="justify">Since the very outset of the Obama presidency, this global military project has become increasingly pervasive, with the reinforcement of US military presence in all major regions of the World  and the development of new advanced weapons systems on an unprecdented scale.</p>\u000A<p>Granting the Nobel Peace Prize to Barack Obama provides legitimacy to the illegal practices of war, to the military occupation of foreign lands, to the relentless killings of civilians in the name of "democracy".</p>\u000A<p align="justify"><img src="http://agabus.com/wp-content/uploads/obama-peace-prize-agabus.jpg" alt="http://agabus.com/wp-content/uploads/obama-peace-prize-agabus.jpg" width="700" height="407" /></p>\u000A<p align="justify">\u000A<p align="justify"><em>[ " ... decision stuns many because he took office less than two weeks before nomination deadline " ...  ]</em></p>\u000A<blockquote>\u000A<p align="justify">\u000A</blockquote>\u000A<p>Both the Obama administration and NATO are directly threatening Russia, China and Iran. The US under Obama is developing "a First Strike Global Missile Shield System":</p>\u000A<p>"Along with space-based weapons, the Airborne Laser is the next defense frontier. ... Never has Ronald Reagan's dream of layered missile defenses - Star Wars, for short - been as....close, at least technologically, to becoming realized."</p>\u000A<p>Reacting to this consolidation, streamlining and upgrading of American global nuclear strike potential, on August 11 the Commander-in-Chief of the Russian Air Force, the same Alexander Zelin cited earlier on the threat of U.S. strikes from space on all of his nation, said that the "Russian Air Force is preparing to meet the threats resulting from the creation of the Global Strike Command in the U.S. Air Force" and that Russia is developing "appropriate systems to meet the threats that may arise." (Rick Rozoff, Showdown with Russia and China: U.S. Advances First Strike Global Missile Shield System, Global Research, August 19, 2009)</p>\u000A<p>At no time since the Cuban missile crisis has the World been closer to the unthinkable: a World War III scenario, a global military conflict involving the use of nuclear weapons.</p>\u000A<p>1. The so-called missile defense shield or Star Wars initiative involving the first strike use of nuclear weapons is now to be developed globally in different regions of the World. The missile shield is largely directed against Russia, China, Iran and North Korea.</p>\u000A<p>2. New US military bases have been set up with a view to establishing US spheres of influence in every region of the World as well as surrounding and confronting Russia and China.</p>\u000A<p>3. There has been an escalation in the Central Asian Middle East war. The "defense budget" under Obama has spiraled with increased allocations to both Afghanistan and Iraq.</p>\u000A<p>4.  Under orders of president Obama, acting as Commander in Chief, Pakistan is now the object of routine US aerial bombardments in violation of its territorial sovereignty, using the "Global War on Terrorism" as a justification.</p>\u000A<p>5. The construction of new military bases is envisaged in Latin America including Colombia on the immediate border of Venezuela.</p>\u000A<p>6. Military aid to Israel has increased. The Obama presidency has expressed its unbending support for Israel and the Israeli military. Obama has remained mum on the atrocities committed by Israel in Gaza. There has not even been a semblance of renewed Israeli-Palestinian negotiations.</p>\u000A<p>7. There has been a reinforcement of the new regional commands including AFRICOM and SOUTHCOM</p>\u000A<p>8. A new round of threats has been directed against Iran.</p>\u000A<p>9. The US is intent upon fostering further divisions between Pakistan and India, which could lead to a regional war, as well as using India's nuclear arsenal as an indirect means to threaten China.</p>\u000A<p>The diabolical nature of this military project was outlined in the 2000 Project for a New American Century (PNAC). The PNAC's declared objectives are:</p>\u000A<p>defend the American homeland;</p>\u000A<p>fight and decisively win multiple, simultaneous major theater wars;</p>\u000A<p>perform the "constabulary" duties associated with shaping the security environment in critical regions;</p>\u000A<p>transform U.S. forces to exploit the "revolution in military affairs;" (Project for a New American Century, Rebuilding Americas Defenses.pdf, September 2000)</p>\u000A<p>The "Revolution in Military Affairs" refers to the development of new advanced weapons systems. The militarization of space, new advanced chemical and biological weapons, sophisticated laser guided missiles, bunker buster bombs, not to mention the US Air Force's climatic warfare program (HAARP) based in Gokona, Alaska, are part of Obama's  "humanitarian arsenal".</p>\u000A<p><span class="outline"><img id="fullSizedImage" class="media" src="http://i282.photobucket.com/albums/kk271/blastform/antennae_haarp.jpg" alt="antennae_haarp.jpg image by blastform" width="707" height="530" /></span></p>\u000A<p><span><strong>War against the Truth</strong></span></p>\u000A<p>This is a war against the truth.  When war becomes peace, the world is turned upside down. Conceptualization is no longer possible.  An inquisitorial social system emerges.</p>\u000A<p>An understanding of fundamental social and political events is replaced by a World of sheer fantasy, where "evil folks" are lurking. The objective of the "Global War on Terrorism" which has been fully endorsed by Obama administration, has been to galvanize public support for a Worldwide campaign against heresy.</p>\u000A<p>In the eyes of public opinion, possessing a "just cause" for waging war is central. A war is said to be Just if it is waged on moral, religious or ethical grounds. The consensus is to wage war. People can longer think for themselves. They accept the authority and  wisdom of the established social order.</p>\u000A<p>The Nobel Committee says that President Obama has given the world "hope for a better future." The prize is awarded for Obama's</p>\u000A<p>"extraordinary efforts to strengthen international diplomacy and cooperation between peoples. The Committee has attached special importance to Obama's vision of and work for a world without nuclear weapons."</p>\u000A<p>...His diplomacy is founded in the concept that those who are to lead the world must do so on the basis of values and attitudes that are shared by the majority of the world's population. (Nobel Press Release, October 9, 2009)</p>\u000A<p>The granting of the Nobel "peace prize" to president Barack Obama has become an integral part of the Pentagon's propaganda machine. It provides a human face to the invaders, it upholds the demonization of those who oppose US military intervention.</p>\u000A<p>The decision to grant Obama the Nobel  Peace Prize was no doubt carefully negotiated with the Norwegian Committee at the highest levels of the US government. It has far reaching implications.</p>\u000A<p>It unequivocally upholds the US led war as a "Just Cause". It erases the war crimes committed both by the Bush and Obama administrations.</p>\u000A<p><img src="http://blog.syracuse.com/following-orion/2008/11/DSCF2005.JPG" alt="http://blog.syracuse.com/following-orion/2008/11/DSCF2005.JPG" width="734" height="551" /></p>\u000A<p><strong><span>War Propaganda:  Jus ad Bellum</span></strong></p>\u000A<p>The "Just war" theory serves to camouflage the nature of US foreign policy, while providing a human face to the invaders.</p>\u000A<p>In both its classical and contemporary versions, the Just war theory upholds war as a "humanitarian operation". It calls for military intervention on ethical and moral grounds against "insurgents", "terrorists", "failed" or "rogue states".</p>\u000A<p>The Just War has been heralded by the Nobel Committee as an instrument of Peace. Obama personifies the "Just War".</p>\u000A<p>Taught in US military academies, a modern-day version of the "Just War" theory has been embodied into US military doctrine. The "war on terrorism" and the notion of "preemption" are predicated on the right to "self defense." They define "when it is permissible to wage war": jus ad bellum.</p>\u000A<p>Jus ad bellum has served to build a consensus within the Armed Forces command structures. It has also served to convince the troops that they are fighting for a "just cause". More generally, the Just War theory in its modern day version is an integral part of war propaganda and media disinformation, applied to gain public support for a war agenda. Under Obama as Nobel Peace Laureate, the Just War becomes universally accepted, upheld by the so-called international community.</p>\u000A<p><em>[NB:  the term \u201Cinternational community\u201D is shorthand for the US, Israel, and Europe - a handful of arrogant and rich countries that oppress the rest of the world ]</em></p>\u000A<p>The ultimate objective is to subdue the citizens, totally depoliticize social life in America, prevent people from thinking and conceptualizing, from analyzing facts and challenging the legitimacy of the US NATO led war.</p>\u000A<p><img src="http://www.metc.net/img/cable%20page.jpg" alt="http://www.metc.net/img/cable%20page.jpg" width="724" height="480" /></p>\u000A<p>War becomes peace, a worthwhile "humanitarian undertaking",  Peaceful dissent becomes heresy.</p>\u000A<p>Military Escalation with a Human Face. Nobel Committee grants the "Green Light"</p>\u000A<p>More significantly, the Nobel peace prize grants legitimacy to an unprecedented  "escalation"  of US-NATO led military operations under the banner of peacemaking.</p>\u000A<p>It contributes to falsifying the nature of the US-NATO military agenda.</p>\u000A<p>Between 40,000 to 60,000 more US and allied troops are to be sent to Afghanistan under a peacemaking banner. On the 8th of October, a day prior to the Nobel Committee's decision, the US Congress granted Obama a 680-billion-dollar defense authorization bill, which is slated to finance the process of military escalation:</p>\u000A<p>"Washington and its NATO allies are planning an unprecedented increase of troops for the war in Afghanistan, even in addition to the 17,000 new American and several thousand NATO forces that have been committed to the war so far this year".</p>\u000A<p><img src="http://images.teamsugar.com/files/upl1/10/104169/33_2008/82293844.preview.jpg" alt="http://images.teamsugar.com/files/upl1/10/104169/33_2008/82293844.preview.jpg" width="715" height="475" /></p>\u000A<p>The number, based on as yet unsubstantiated reports of what U.S. and NATO commander Stanley McChrystal and the chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff Michael Mullen have demanded of the White House, range from 10,000 to 45,000.</p>\u000A<p>Fox News has cited figures as high as 45,000 more American soldiers and ABC News as many as 40,000. On September 15 the Christian Science Monitor wrote of "perhaps as many as 45,000."</p>\u000A<p>The similarity of the estimates indicate that a number has been agreed upon and America's obedient media is preparing domestic audiences for the possibility of the largest escalation of foreign armed forces in Afghanistan's history. Only seven years ago the United States had 5,000 troops in the country, but was scheduled to have 68,000 by December even before the reports of new deployments surfaced. (Rick Rozoff, U.S., NATO Poised For Most Massive War In Afghanistan's History, Global Research, September 24, 2009)</p>\u000A<p>Within hours of the decision of the Norwegian Nobel committee, Obama met with the War Council, or should we call it the "Peace Council". This meeting had been carefully scheduled to coincide with that of the Norwegian Nobel committee.</p>\u000A<p>This key meeting behind closed doors in the Situation Room of the White House included Vice President Joe Biden, Secretary of State Hillary Clinton, Secretary of Defense Robert Gates, and key political and military advisers. General  Stanley McChrystal participated in the meeting via video link from Kabul.</p>\u000A<p>General Stanley McChrystal is said to have offered the Commander in Chief "several alternative options" "including a maximum injection of 60,000 extra troops". The 60,000 figure was quoted following a leak of the Wall Street Journal (AFP: After Nobel nod, Obama convenes Afghan war council, October 9, 2009)</p>\u000A<p><img src="http://news.soc.mil/releases/News%20Archive/2004/04MAR/040313-F-2828D-201.jpg" alt="http://news.soc.mil/releases/News%20Archive/2004/04MAR/040313-F-2828D-201.jpg" width="949" height="618" /></p>\u000A<p><em>[ A photo of some hired killers getting off a C-5 Galaxy - one of the world's largest aircraft ]</em></p>\u000A<p>"The president had a robust conversation about the security and political challenges in Afghanistan and the options for building a strategic approach going forward," according to an administration official (quoted in AFP: After Nobel nod, Obama convenes Afghan war council  October 9, 2009)</p>\u000A<p>The Nobel committee had in a sense given Obama a green light.  The October 9 meeting in the Situation Room was to set the groundwork for a further escalation of the conflict under the banner of counterinsurgency and democracy building.</p>\u000A<p>Meanwhile, in the course of the last few months, US forces have stepped up their aerial bombardments of village communities in the northern tribal areas of Pakistan, under the banner of combating Al Qaeda.</p>

VAn Open Letter To American Express
p350
sg5
Vhttp://uncensored.co.nz/2009/10/27/an-open-letter-to-american-express/
p351
sg7
(lp352
sg9
V<p>Dear American Express,</p>\u000A<p>How are you? I know how hard this global recession has been on everyone, so I thought I\u2019d check in on an old friend. We <em>have</em> had a professional relationship for over ten years.</p>\u000A<p>Me? Well, I\u2019m getting by. Several months ago, I was laid off with millions of other people. I had to take a job at half my prior salary and sell my house. But what am I saying? You know all this! That\u2019s right. After you saw that my credit report showed a sudden three month hiccup in my otherwise flawless finances, you called to see how I was doing. No wait. Not to see how I was doing. To unilaterally cut my credit limit from $25,000 to $1,000. Oh, and you didn\u2019t actually call. But that post card was nice.</p>\u000A<p align="center"><img src="http://cdn-i.dmdentertainment.com/funpages/cms_content/18076/amex.jpg" alt="" /></p>\u000A<p>Needless to say, this rift in our friendship left me spinning with questions. Mostly, I just want to know why. I was so good to you. I mean, yes I stopped paying my mortgage, (for the house already on the market) but I paid every single other bill. I paid all YOUR bills. Remember the good times? You were my friend \u2026 with benefits. What happened to the American Express I knew? The one who thanked me for my prompt payments and kept raising my credit limit? I got a new job. Is it my ass? It\u2019s not me. It\u2019s these new jeans. Ask Capital One, they\u2019re totally into what I got going on. It just seemed like someone over there had made a grievous error.</p>\u000A<p>So I decided to call because that\u2019s what friends do, right? They don\u2019t jump to conclusions and take rash actions without the facts. But, apparently, it wasn\u2019t an error. One of your employees \u2013let\u2019s call her BitchFace\u2014 conveyed the sentiment in a subtle way:</p>\u000A<p><img src="http://i175.photobucket.com/albums/w148/wgladstone/mr_snibbles.jpg" alt="" />\u201CIt\u2019s not an error, Mr. Gladstone,\u201D she said, twisting her heel into the larynx of a baby chihuahua. As I bent over to see if I could find what was left of my self worth and dignity rolling away on the floor, she upped the ante:</p>\u000A<p>\u201CWe have you right where we want you.\u201D</p>\u000A<p>Yeah, I\u2019m not joking. Who says that? I think she meant Amex had me at their desired credit limit, but seriously? \u201CWe have you right where we want you\u201D is third on the list of evil phrases right behind \u201Cwe have ways of making you talk,\u201D and \u201Cwe\u2019re going to revoke your Facebook account if you keep harassing teens.\u201D</p>\u000A<p>I\u2019m not going to lie to you American Express. This was a serious test of our friendship. But once my credit report was updated it showed no mortgage debt. Indeed, I had a credit rating of over 700. I faxed you the new information, proudly. Glad that we\u2019d be able to put all this nonsense behind us, and you\u2019d be able to return my credit limit to a point higher than let\u2019s say \u2026 the cost of a high def TV or 8 nice dinners? I mean, c\u2019mon, with a $1,000 credit limit, how was I going to afford a quality hit man to kill each and every one of the miserable bastards I\u2019d spoken to at your company? I\u2019d have to use some untested soldier of fortune off craigslist and he might not be any good. He might not slice your carotid artery clean enough and you\u2019d have to die slowly over a long period of time while he did unspeakably perverted things to your increasingly lifeless corpse. None of us wanted that. So I submitted hard evidence and waited for you to do the right thing.</p>\u000A<p>Well guess what? For a cynical guy who does a <a href="http://www.cracked.com/video_17618_black-eyed-peas-have-officially-written-worst-song-ever.html">web series about hating things that suck</a>, I am surprisingly optimistic and naive. Two weeks after my financial care package you sent another post card (I guess BitchFace couldn\u2019t come to the phone) informing me that you were keeping my credit limit at $1,000.</p>\u000A<p>One thing did make me feel a little better, though. No, not the new friend I found online who is willing to torture/murder creditors for half his normal rates (although that <em>does</em> help) but finding out that I\u2019m not alone.  <a href="http://www.boston.com/business/personalfinance/articles/2009/01/31/lenders_abruptly_cut_lines_of_credit/">American Express and other credit card companies have been up to all sorts of mindless shenanigans</a>, making draconian decisions based more on the appearances of cutting costs than actually understanding which clients present unreasonable risks.</p>\u000A<p>But hey, these are tough times. I get it. And I think it\u2019s completely fair that you safeguard yourself against greed and carelessness. Even if it was your greed and carelessness that put you in this situation in the first place. If making my life more difficult helps you sleep at night, then, hey, I guess that\u2019s what friends are for.</p>\u000A<p>Besides, I\u2019m very much into the idea of you sleeping soundly. My new friend tells me he works best at night.</p>\u000A<p>Wishing you every success.</p>\u000A<p>Your pal,</p>\u000A<p>Gladstone</p>\u000A<p><a href="http://www.cracked.com/blog/?p=12808">Source</a></p>

You have managed to create an imaginative display out of breathing human beings \u2013 turning them into savages and barbarians while they do nothing less than defend their lives against imperialistic aggression.<br />\u000ASplashing pictures of armed Iraqi\u2019s with masks on sends the Conservative populace of America reeling while pictures of American soldiers in tanks,donning their uniforms makes them proud.</span></p></blockquote>\u000A<p><span>The American flag makes everything pretty and easier to swallow. VHide the new Facebook Suggestion Box
p373

V<p>Tired of Facebook telling you to reconnect with an ex, someone who has passed away or a family member you talk with every day but just not on Facebook? Don't like being told to write on someone's wall?  Or being told to help find more friends for your mom?</p>\u000A<p>This hides the new Facebook suggestions box.</p>\u000A<p><strong>Instructions for Firefox:</strong></p>\u000A<ol>\u000A<li>Install this Firefox extension: <a href="https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/2108">https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/2108</a></li>\u000A<li>Restart Firefox</li>\u000A<li>Click on the button saying \u201Cload into stylish\u201D on this webpage: <a href="http://userstyles.org/styles/22130">http://userstyles.org/styles/22130</a></li>\u000A</ol>\u000A<p><strong>Instructions for Internet Explorer 7:</strong></p>\u000A<ol>\u000A<li>Save this file somewhere on your computer: <a href="http://www.cre8d-design.com/wp-content/uploads/2009/10/hidefacebooksuggestionsbox.css">hidefacebooksuggestionsbox.css</a></li>\u000A<li>In Internet Explorer, select the <strong>Tools menu</strong> and then <strong>Internet Options</strong></li>\u000A<li>On the General tab click on the <strong>Accessibility</strong> button</li>\u000A<li>Tick <strong>Format documents using my style sheet</strong></li>\u000A<li>Click on the <strong>Browse</strong> button and find the file you downloaded, <code>hidefacebooksuggestionsbox.css</code> and click OK.</li>\u000A</ol>\u000A<p>That\u2019s it!</p>\u000A<p>Enjoy.</p>\u000A<div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/cre8ddesign?a=PEAyzjlDhCw:nRWYGb03t9M:D7DqB2pKExk"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/cre8ddesign?i=PEAyzjlDhCw:nRWYGb03t9M:D7DqB2pKExk" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/cre8ddesign?a=PEAyzjlDhCw:nRWYGb03t9M:V_sGLiPBpWU"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/cre8ddesign?i=PEAyzjlDhCw:nRWYGb03t9M:V_sGLiPBpWU" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/cre8ddesign?a=PEAyzjlDhCw:nRWYGb03t9M:F7zBnMyn0Lo"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/cre8ddesign?i=PEAyzjlDhCw:nRWYGb03t9M:F7zBnMyn0Lo" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div>

VPaul Graham: Priority Access to Twitter Is Practical Necessity
p412
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/Dk0bRO6rfus/says-paul-graham-twitter-is-th.php
p413
sg7
(lp414
sg9
V<p><img alt="paulgraham_ycombinator_oct09.jpg" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/readwritestart/images/paulgraham_ycombinator_oct09.jpg" width="150" height="161" />If hardcore hackers had any doubts whether the real-time web was a legitimate development environment, <a href="http://ycombinator.com">Y Combinator</a> co-founder Paul Graham is dispelling them. In an interview with Graham, ReadWriteWeb learned that the entrepreneur-turned-investor issued a "Request for Startups" (RFS) asking for ideas from companies utilizing <a href="http://ycombinator.com/rfs3.html">Twitter</a> and <a href="http://ycombinator.com/rfs4.html">Justin.tv's live video API</a>. Groups who are accepted to Y-Combinator and fall under these categories will be given "priority access" to Twitter and Justin.tv. </p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16900&cb=16900" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16900&n=16900" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<p>Says Graham, "In the beginning people believed Twitter was a fad and they didn't realize this was a new protocol...In some ways Twitter is a replacement for email. We're not doing this to promote Twitter, we generally believe it's important."</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img alt="ycombinator_RFS_oct09a.jpg" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/readwritestart/images/ycombinator_RFS_oct09a.jpg" width="510" height="390" /></p>\u000A\u000A<p>It's obvious why Y Combinator companies are able to gain special support from Justin.tv's founders. The lifecasting site took on Y Combinator seed funding in 2007 and has since developed into one of the web's leading online video destinations. The Twitter partnership is a different story. While it's important that Y Combinator teams have Twitter's support, the question on many people's minds is, "If Twitter is an all-important protocol, then why should one group of investors get privileged access to its data-rich firehose?"</p>\u000A\u000A<p>According to Graham, "This is a practical matter. They need to be able to keep ahead of growth technically... If thousands of startups want to talk to you, then you need to have filters. Even before publishing this Request for Startups, we had a dedicated guy at Twitter who answered Y Combinator questions." </p>\u000A\u000A<p>In the past, Y Combinator-funded real-time meta-search engine <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/scoopler_real-time_meta-search_for_twitter_digg_de.php">Scoopler</a> worked closely with Twitter.  </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Said Graham, "Honestly, Twitter probably has a lot of filters on those who access them. The only thing special about this is that we formalized it with an RFS." </p>\u000A\u000A<p>After taking a $2 million dollar investment from Sequoia Capital in March, Y Combinator <a href="http://ycombinator.com/party.html">aims to increase its portfolio companies from 40 to roughly 60 per year</a>. The "Request for Startups" offers companies direction in their applications. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Graham notes that when individuals apply for Y Combinator, they are asked to specify if they are applying with an RFS in mind. While he estimates that only 10% of applications are directly related to the RFS, he believes that many who might not apply are inspired to do so after seeing their ideas highlighted. The incubator's first requests were issued in August with a call for alternative <a href="http://ycombinator.com/rfs1.html"> journalism</a> and <a href="http://ycombinator.com/rfs2.html">online retail</a> ideas.</p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/readwritestart/2009/10/says-paul-graham-twitter-is-th.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/fkMXg0TUObiA7kIJjMespR1hPww/0/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/fkMXg0TUObiA7kIJjMespR1hPww/0/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a><br />\u000A<a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/fkMXg0TUObiA7kIJjMespR1hPww/1/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/fkMXg0TUObiA7kIJjMespR1hPww/1/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=Dk0bRO6rfus:nvRqpy5-wo4:FFnlKYwJmN0"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?d=C2pbw5bZMiI" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=Dk0bRO6rfus:nvRqpy5-wo4:yIl2AUoC8zA"><img VIBM: You Can't Squeeze Knowledge From a Pixel
p421

Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/had-c-q8doI/ibms-identity-insight-server-y.php

VAutomattic Open Sources Natural Language Spell-Checker After the Deadline
p428
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/d5rVsU9o9Gw/automattic_open_sources_natural_language_spell-che.php
p429
sg7
(lp430
sg9
V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/readwritestart/wp-atd.jpg" />Matt Mullenweg has just annouced on his <a href="http://ma.tt/2009/10/atd-now-os/">blog</a> that WordPress parent company Automattic is open sourcing After the Deadline, a natural-language spell-checking plugin for WordPress and TinyMCE that was only recently ushered into the Automattic fold.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Scarcely seven weeks after its acquisition was <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/readwritestart/2009/09/natural-language-spellchecker-after.php">announced</a>, After the Deadline's core technology is being released under the GPL. Moreover, writes Mullenweg, "There's also a new jQuery API that makes it easy to integrate with any text area."</p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16899&cb=16899" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16899&n=16899" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<p>AtD founder, former military researcher, and Y-Combinator reject Rafael Mudge noted at the acquisition that he intended to continue his natural language processing research and expand support to other languages. He <a href="http://blog.afterthedeadline.com/2009/09/08/after-the-deadline-acquired/">wrote</a>, "We hope to see others build on the service... We're planning to open source the After the Deadline engine and the rule-sets that go with it. This will be the most comprehensive proofreading suite available under an open source license."</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The related API is the same one that powers a plugin from another Automattic property, <a href="http://www.intensedebate.com/">Intense Debate</a>. Mudge told <a href="http://ostatic.com/blog/after-the-deadline-language-checking-software-used-by-wordpress-now-open-source">Ostatic</a>, "I'd like to see AtD spread as far and wide as possible. I'm an inventor first and have this desire to see my inventions help people."</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Interested parties can check out this <a href="http://www.polishmywriting.com/">demo</a> or read the tech overview and grab the source code <a href="http://open.afterthedeadline.com/">here</a>.</p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/automattic_open_sources_natural_language_spell-che.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a VBusiness Intelligence and Analytics Hot Topics at IBM Information on Demand Conference
p435
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/lq2pOV3cgtQ/we-are-here-at-the.php
p436
sg7
(lp437
sg9
V<p><img alt="ibmiod.png" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/enterprise/assets_c/2009/10/ibmiod-thumb-150x48-10001.png" width="150" height="48" />Business intelligence, analytics and the demand for process optimization are the big draws here at the<a href="http://www-01.ibm.com/software/data/conf/"> IBM Information On Demand Conference</a> in Las Vegas.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>As one executive said on stage, its not enough to react quickly to what is happening but to predict it.</p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16898&cb=16898" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16898&n=16898" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<p>According to IBM's CIO Global Study, 83 percent of respondents said business intelligence and analytics are a top priority. IBM sees business analytics as the next mega trend, growing twice as fast as the rest of the IT industry.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>For example, <a href="http://www-01.ibm.com/software/data/conf/cognos.html"> Cognos,</a> acquired by IBM in 2007, is now a hub for IBM's business intelligence offerings.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Cognos announced its Content Analytics product at the conference. With the addition, Cognos is putting an emphasis on combining a client's internal data with external information to provide a more complete picture of the market and how to optimize marketing and processes within the organization.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img alt="contentanalytics2.jpg" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/enterprise/assets_c/2009/10/contentanalytics2-thumb-600x392-9998.jpg" width="600" height="392" class="mt-image-none" /></p>\u000A\u000A<p>This may be used to correlate transaction information with unstructured information that the client collects from the web.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Applications may include using analytics for sales purposes to get a better understanding and deeper insights into trends that come as trickles from actual purchases. The information can be analyzed with other data from sales reps about the products they are selling. This information can then be used by sales executives to predict trends and ready the rest of the organization for changes in the marketplace.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>But though this conference is about information on demand, there is little talk about the real-time web. We asked IBM executives if they can integrate activity stream information, such as a Twitter search pertaining to a company name or product. They said it was possible though it is unclear exactly how this would be accomplished. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Most of the examples we saw with Cognos Content Analytics focused on massive amounts of form data that can be viewed in a dashboard. That's impressive but we would like to see how IBM is leveraging the social web and how they plan to compete against the number of lightweight social technologies that are filling the market.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><em>[Disclosure: IBM paid for a plane ticket and hotel room for Alex Williams to attend the IBM Information On Demand Conference.]</em><br />\u000A</p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/enterprise/2009/10/we-are-here-at-the.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=lq2pOV3cgtQ:rGjbXjy9fn4:FFnlKYwJmN0"><img VAny Given Sunday: 7 Sports Tools You Can't Live Without
p442
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/ypkHZG0DSjc/any-given-sunday-sports-tools.php
p443
sg7
(lp444
sg9
V<p><img alt="sports_lead_oct09.jpg" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/readwritestart/images/sports_lead_oct09.jpg" width="150" height="155" />Touchdown dances, chest painters and rally caps - if you're not a sports fan, it's hard to understand why a perfectly upstanding citizen would wear a gigantic foam hand or engage in the politically incorrect Tomahawk chop. But if you are a diehard sports addict, you've probably been one since you were a kid. We watched in awe when Nolan Ryan pitched a 101 mph fast ball at the age of forty, when Air Jordan effortlessly dunked from the free throw line and when Joe Montana set the record for most yards passing during Super Bowl XIX. When you've been present to watch sports history, you can't turn your back on the game now. Nevertheless, with so much happening at once, below are a few tools that can help you juggle multiple games:</p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16897&cb=16897" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16897&n=16897" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<p>1. <img alt="sports_fanfeedr_oct09.jpg" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/readwritestart/images/sports_fanfeedr_oct09.jpg" width="317" height="477" align="right" /><b><a href="http://lockerblogger.com">Lockerblogger</a></b>: Lockerblogger offers users a chance to create fan profiles and track the sports they're most interested in. Through blogs, video uploads, short messages and in-site chat, the service offers users a chance to connect with sports stars and fans.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>2. <b><a href="http://yardbarker.com">Yardbarker</a></b>:Similar to Lockerblogger, Yardbarker lets fans keep up-to-date with the latest rumors, training news and injuries. With strict league policies arising around Twitter-usage, these services are a great way to get insider news. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>3. <b><a href="http://itunes.apple.com/WebObjects/MZStore.woa/wa/viewSoftware?id=317469184&mt=8">ESPN ScoreCenter</a></b>: This iPhone App offers the official stats and scores on more than 500 sports leagues including the NFL, NHL, NBA and MLB. Users can also follow <a href="http://soccernet.espn.go.com/?cc=5901">Soccernet</a> for soccer scores and news. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>4. <b><a href="http://itunes.apple.com/WebObjects/MZStore.woa/wa/viewSoftware?id=309327900&mt=8">MLB at Bat iPhone App</a></b>: A number of services offer users a chance to listen to regular season games and watch clips. For $10, MLB at Bat offers live video of postseason games streamed via the iPhone. The <a href="http://itunes.apple.com/WebObjects/MZStore.woa/wa/viewSoftware?id=281969989&mt=8">free app</a> offers scores and stats. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>5. <b><a href="http://itunes.apple.com/WebObjects/MZStore.woa/wa/viewSoftware?id=335754275&mt=8">NBA Game Time iPhone App</a></b>: Similar to MLB at Bat, NBA Game Time has both a <a href="http://itunes.apple.com/WebObjects/MZStore.woa/wa/viewSoftware?id=335744614&mt=8">free version with basic scores and info</a> and a <a href="http://itunes.apple.com/WebObjects/MZStore.woa/wa/viewSoftware?id=335754275&mt=8">premium iPhone application</a> with radio broadcasts, video recaps and push notifications to keep tabs on your favorite teams. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>6. <b><a href="http://fanfeedr.com">Fanfeedr</a></b>: ReadWriteWeb first <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/readwritestart/2009/08/fanfeedr-gives-sports-fans-per.php">covered Fanfeedr in mid-August</a>. The site offers a real-time feed of sports-related traditional news reports, blog posts and Twitter updates. The company also offers an <a href="http://itunes.apple.com/WebObjects/MZStore.woa/wa/viewSoftware?id=322441443&mt=8">iPhone app</a> where users can check scores, talk trash with rival fans and follow along with game analysis. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>7. <b><a href="http://www.watercooler-inc.com/">Watercooler</a></b>: Having just raised $5.5 million dollars to expand it's sports-related social games, Watercooler connects more than 40 million fans via Facebook, MySpace and Bebo. Best known for its Facebook <a href="http://www.facebook.com/apps/application.php?id=8250193577">Fantasy Football application</a>, the company creates sports applications for individual teams as well as sports-related networks. </p>\u000A\u000A<p><small><em>Photo Credit: <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/www.flickr.com/photos/sarki/">John Lew</a></em></small></p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/readwritestart/2009/10/any-given-sunday-sports-tools.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/ZXePSE1w_AVsWx7JUe0CBOjMV8U/0/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/ZXePSE1w_AVsWx7JUe0CBOjMV8U/0/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a><br
