VGoogle Search Gets Personal: Social Search Launches in Google Labs
p449
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/KDK95zWhQys/google_search_gets_personal_social_search_launches.php
p450
sg7
(lp451
sg9
V<p><img alt="google_logo_jan_09.jpg" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/google_logo_jan_09.jpg" />Social Search just went <a href="http://googleblog.blogspot.com/2009/10/introducing-google-social-search-i.html">live </a>in <a href="http://www.google.com/experimental/">Google Labs</a>. Google <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/google_social_search_facebook.php">announced</a> that it was working on this Social Search feature at the Web 2.0 Summit last week, but at that time, Google's Marissa Mayer announced that it would only be available "in a few weeks." <font></font>Social Search taps into a user's social network profiles and displays relevant links and status updates that members of a user's own social network have shared at the bottom of the default search results page. According to Google, Social Search will enhance the search experience on Google by providing users with more personally relevant search results.</p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16894&cb=16894" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16894&n=16894" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<p>To get started, you first have to head over to <a href="http://www.google.com/experimental/">Google Labs</a>'s experimental section and activate this feature. For now, Social Search will only be available in the US and in English. </p>\u000A\u000A<p><img alt="google_social_search_nz_example.jpg" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/google_social_search_nz_example.jpg" /></p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Sources: Gmail Contacts, Google Reader Subscriptions and Your Google Profile</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>Social Search can tab into three different sources, so you will need accounts on at least one of these services to make Social Search work. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Social search uses the <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/To get started, you first have to head over to Google Labs&rsquo;s experimental section and activate this feature. ">Gmail contacts</a> you have added to your friends and coworker lists and those you have chatted with on Google Talk. Social search also looks at your&#160;<a href="http://reader.google.com">Google Reader</a> subscriptions and the social networking profiles you have added to your Google Profile. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>While you don't need to have a <a href="http://www.google.com/profiles">Google Profile</a>, this service is a hub for your social networking profile on Social Search. Based on the information in your Google Profile, Google can <a href="http://code.google.com/apis/socialgraph/">auto-detect your social networking profiles</a> and your friends on services like Flickr, FriendFeed, YouTube, Reddit, Digg, del.icio.us, BrightKite and many others. </p>\u000A\u000A<h2>How it Works and How to Trigger Social Search Explicitly</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>Once activated, Social Search results will appear at the bottom of the standard search results page and will be clearly labeled as "results from people in your social circle." As Google's search evangelist Matt Cutts pointed out to us in an interview earlier today, it is important to note that not every search will trigger Social Search results. When it does, however, the results should be highly relevant. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>You can also explicitly trigger Social Search from the <a href="http://googleblog.blogspot.com/2009/05/behind-scenes-of-search-options-panel.html">search options panel</a>. There, Google will now also present a list of your friends that it thinks are the most closely related to the keywords you were searching for. By clicking on a name, you can restrict your search even further and just see results from this one person.</p>\u000A\u000A<p></p>\u000A\u000A<p>&#160;</p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Social Search Makes Google Profiles More Useful</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>This new feature will also put a new emphasis on Google Profiles. Google has made some moves to make these profiles more prominent by highlighting some profiles when users search for people, but Google Profiles has generally not received a lot of attention from users. Now, however, as the hub for Social Search, users have an incentive to fill out their profiles - which, of course, will also give Google more information about you and your social network.</p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Privacy Concerns?</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>We talked to Google Fellow <a href="http://singhal.info/">Amit Singhal</a>, search evangelist <a href="http://www.mattcutts.com/blog/">Matt Cutts</a>, and Maureen Heymans (the Technical Lead for Social Search) and Murali Viswanathan (the Product Manager for Social Search) earlier today and the team was obviously excited about this launch. The Social Search team was especially excited about the fact social search will now make your friends' knowledge far more accessible than ever before and that this will make it easier to find trusted product reviews and local search results.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img alt="social_search_2_oct09.jpg" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/social_search_2_oct09.jpg" /></p>\u000A\u000A<p>We also asked the team about how they thought users would react to the fact that Google indexes and surfaces all of their social networking profiles and connections, which could spark some privacy concerns. In reaction to this, Matt Cutts pointed out that all of the info that Google indexes is already publically available on the Internet, including a user's friend connections. He also stressed that this was an opt-in experiment.</p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Social Search as "A Big Chess Move Against Facebook"</h2>\u000A\u000A<p><div><a name="fb_share" type="box_count"></a></div>As our own Marshall Kirkpatrick pointed out <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/google_social_search_facebook.php">last week</a>, Social Search can also be seen as a "big chess move against Facebook." Both Google and Facebook want users to come to their sites to see what their friends are saying about a given topic. Google, however, can't tap into your social circle on Facebook and hence won't be able to highlight status updates from your Facebook friends, which explains why Google needed to <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/google_indexes_twitter.php">make a deal with Twitter</a> to get access to status updates from their service.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img alt="social_search_real_time_example.jpg" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/social_search_real_time_example.jpg" /></p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/google_search_gets_personal_social_search_launches.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/jqAimhJMyavX7gV_TBc932lh-p8/0/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/jqAimhJMyavX7gV_TBc932lh-p8/0/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a><br />\u000A<a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/jqAimhJMyavX7gV_TBc932lh-p8/1/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/jqAimhJMyavX7gV_TBc932lh-p8/1/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=KDK95zWhQys:qKNq0c-OlH4:FFnlKYwJmN0"><img VYour Augmented Future: The 3 Hottest Videos From International AR Symposium
p456
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/NDlpH98Wg_8/cool_augmented_reality_videos.php
p457
sg7
(lp458
sg9
V<p><img alt="eyepet150.jpg" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/eyepet150.jpg" width="150" height="139" />3D virtual pets to hold in your hand and interact with, software that turns drawn objects into movable 3D objects subject to the laws of physics and a Microsoft hiring-coup.  Those are the stories behind the hottest videos from the eye and brain-candy world of Augmented Reality, as seen at last week's <a href="http://www.ismar09.org/">International Symposium on Augmented and Extended Reality</a> in Orlando, Florida.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Who says the web is all about <em>pages</em> that you view in a <em>browser</em>?  Check out these three visions of a fast-approaching future where data is drawn from and overlaid on top of the real world around us.</p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16895&cb=16895" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16895&n=16895" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Kid Stuff: Eye Pet</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>The <a href="http://www.eyepet.com/">Eye Pet</a> is a virtual critter that you can interact with through a webcam on your computer.  Check out this demo where the Sony Computer Entertainment Europe pets the animal and spins through a 3D menu of toys to play use in playing with it.  It's pretty awesome.  The Eye Pet is expected to be released <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xRBAlSxinL4&NR=1">for the PS3 game system</a> as early as next month.</p>\u000A\u000A<p></p>\u000A\u000A<p>That looks like a lot of fun for kids (who knows about the psychological impact) but imagine other interactive 3D objects with menus of options like this.  Occupational training possibilities?  Sports practice?  There seems to be a lot of possibilities.  </p>\u000A\u000A<p><em>Thanks to Canadian PhD student <a href="http://compscigail.blogspot.com/">Gail Carmichael</a> for shooting that video.</em></p>\u000A\u000A<h2>The New AR Paradigm: AR Sketch</h2>\u000A\u000A<p></p>\u000A\u000A<p>We <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/iphone_augmented_reality_hack.php">wrote about this international project last week</a> and the team behind it went on to win the Best Student Paper award at the ISMAR conference.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>AR Sketch takes drawn images, processes live video capture of the drawings and turns them into 3D image overlays.  Then it subjects them to a physics simulation.  The team behind it just happened to hack into the private API for live video processing on the iPhone and make it available to developers around the world, too. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Popular AR apps like Yelp or Layar on mobile phones don't actually know what they are looking at, they just know where you are and which direction you're facing.  Thus they can tell you what they believe you're looking at.  Marker-based AR apps know only to look for one thing - a printed marker with a pattern on it that triggers display of an overlay.  Sketch AR needs neither guesses nor markers - it processes  and augments what you're actually looking at.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>It's nuts.  As Ori Inbar wrote about the Sketch AR team in <a href="http://gamesalfresco.com/2009/10/23/ismar-2009-epilogue-a-new-augmented-reality-world-order/">an overview of ISMAR</a>, "Their work is revolutionizing the AR world by avoiding the need to print markers - or any images whatsoever."</p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Here Comes Microsoft AR!</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>Oxford's <a href="http://www.robots.ox.ac.uk/~gk/">Georg Klein</a>, whom Inbar calls "the smartest Computer Vision guy on the block," just joined Microsoft this month, conference-goers learned.  Is Microsoft going to make a major Augmented Reality play?  They'd be fools not to explore the possibility.  They don't want to be left out in the cold if AR does become the next version of the web.  Here's what their new man's been working on.</p>\u000A\u000A<p></p>\u000A\u000A<p><a href="http://www.vuzix.com/iwear/products_wrap310.html"><img alt="wrap310.jpg" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/wrap310.jpg" width="325" height="189" align="right" hspace="5px" vspace="5px" /></a>These exciting examples of Augmented Reality have little to do with mobile location awareness, a nice reminder that there's a whole lot more to the field.  Mobile AR browsers are the best known commercial services so far, but academic research on other forms of AR has been going on for years.  </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Ready to browse and interact with data on top of the physical world, through webcams, mobile phones and increasingly <a href="http://www.vuzix.com/iwear/products_wrap310.html">svelte AR glasses</a>? A future when such experiences are mainstream may be fast approaching.</p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/cool_augmented_reality_videos.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/-deNOzQjVE_eF5akvZWQLmYSb9w/0/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/-deNOzQjVE_eF5akvZWQLmYSb9w/0/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a><br />\u000A<a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/-deNOzQjVE_eF5akvZWQLmYSb9w/1/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/-deNOzQjVE_eF5akvZWQLmYSb9w/1/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=NDlpH98Wg_8:C9Z39wp3pf0:FFnlKYwJmN0"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?d=FFnlKYwJmN0" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=NDlpH98Wg_8:C9Z39wp3pf0:Ij26kaj3iuU"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?d=Ij26kaj3iuU" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=NDlpH98Wg_8:C9Z39wp3pf0:C2pbw5bZMiI"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?d=C2pbw5bZMiI" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=NDlpH98Wg_8:C9Z39wp3pf0:yIl2AUoC8zA"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?i=NDlpH98Wg_8:C9Z39wp3pf0:V_sGLiPBpWU" border="0" /></a> <a /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=NDlpH98Wg_8:C9Z39wp3pf0:F7zBnMyn0Lo"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?i=NDlpH98Wg_8:C9Z39wp3pf0:F7zBnMyn0Lo" VGetGlue.com: Distributed Networking & Recommendations Made Simple & Fun
p463
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/FndgulQT6p8/getgluecom_distributed_networking_recommendation.php
p464
sg7
(lp465
sg9
V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/getglue.jpg" />Once just a browser add-on that allowed users to surf smarter across several verticals, AdaptiveBlue's <a href="http://getglue.com">Glue</a> is now a site-centric product that acts as both a hub and a spoke of the social web.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Glue's <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/echo_creator_khris_loux_on_the_ties_that_bind_the.php">synaptic web</a>-esque technology is based on a user's browsing across common sites such as Amazon, Wikipedia and YouTube, and those visits and any interactions (comments, "likes," etc.) feeding back to automatically create a taste profile and a web of affinity with other users and recommendations of other items or content across about a dozen categories, including music, books and movies. So, can this be done without violating users' privacy or - worse yet - frustrating and boring them into attrition?</p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16893&cb=16893" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16893&n=16893" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<p><em>[Disclosure: AdaptiveBlue founder and CEO Alex Iskold is a ReadWriteWeb writer.]</em></p>\u000A\u000A<p>AdaptiveBlue VP Fraser Kelton thinks both aims can be accomplished. In a phone interview this morning, he shared that Glue has a three-tiered set of privacy controls to ensure that items are shared only when a user wants them to be. As the privacy/permissions inverse of Facebook Beacon, an <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/facebook_beacon_apology.php">ill-fated</a> system for socially powered product recommendation, the Glue system is completely opt-in for users and opt-out for publishers.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/glue1.jpg" /><em>Glue's all-new user profiles are rolling out today at GetGlue.com.</em></p>\u000A\u000A<p><br />\u000A"Nobody's confortable sharing all of their stream," said Kelton. "Financial sites, adult content - we don't want any of that stuff shared." In addition to having a set list of sites from which to pull browsing and interaction data, Kelton said, "The secondary privacy controls can prevent visits to a website from being shared unless the user has a specific interaction on that site. You can also opt to have a private profile so only your friends can see the items you interact with." Finally, Kelton told us that users can delete or edit their own shared content on an item-by-item basis.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Our other concern was whether Glue would be a semantic web geek-fest or whether the average end user would also be able to use, enjoy, and return to the site. Kelton said the site went over well with non-techie beta testers, many of whom started out using the GetGlue.com website and eventually also installed the add-on for an even richer experience.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>One of the factors we think makes Glue so much fun for end users, from geeks to complete Luddites, is its Foursquare-like system of achievement and rewards. "We're big fans of game interaction driving the user experience," said Kelton, who also revealed that the product team considered Xbox 360 as inspiration for the Glue system. Users can earn stickers on their profiles based on how many items they browse or interact with, how many users discover content through them, and how much of an expert they are on a particular topic.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/glue2.jpg" /><em>Glue's game-like system of badges or stickers as rewards for user interactions and discovery makes for addictive browsing.</em></p>\u000A\u000A<p>Each item indexed by Glue can have a guru, and only one guru at a time. The result is friendly competition, increased interactions and a very sticky website that's compelling and entertaining for even the least technical end user.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The site also allows for content to be pushed to a user's existing social networks, such as Facebook and Twitter. Here's a demo video showing more about how the site works:</p>\u000A\u000A<p></p>\u000A\u000A<p>As previously mentioned, the user experience of Glue - both the site and the revamped add-on - is one of synapses and nodes, not back-and-forth browsing and search for content. As data and content from all around the web is associated with films, books, music, and other items, users are able to quickly scan and consume related content without further navigation. This type of curated experience is something the AdaptiveBlue team calls "shortcut search."</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/glue3.jpg" /><em>As a social network, GetGlue.com is a hub; but the way it curates content makes it a series of spokes, as well.</em></p>\u000A\u000A<p>"You don't have to go to Rotten Tomatoes or YouTube. We know there's a subset of information users want, and we're bringing it in," said Kelton, who is very excited about Glue's position on distributed social networking and the semantic web. "Jeremiah [Owyang] uses the term 'social colonization.' I also think we're implementing what Charlene Li talks about when she uses the phrase, 'The network is all around us.'"</p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/getgluecom_distributed_networking_recommendation.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/8tYp-cw7sKsu0DkEp2MFYJz-F6w/0/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/8tYp-cw7sKsu0DkEp2MFYJz-F6w/0/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a><br />\u000A<a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/8tYp-cw7sKsu0DkEp2MFYJz-F6w/1/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/8tYp-cw7sKsu0DkEp2MFYJz-F6w/1/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=FndgulQT6p8:we4hwdbELI4:FFnlKYwJmN0"><img VFacebook Launches Live Counts & Stats for Sharing Widget
p470
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/M0JdDNlOPHU/facebook_launches_live_counts_for_sharing_widget.php

V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/fb-share.jpg" />Joining the ranks of tools such as Tweetmeme and Digg widgets, Facebook's Share button will now be showing the number of users who share items in real time - and with a new set of analytics features.</p>\u000A\u000A<div><a name="fb_share" type="box_count"></a></div>\u000A\u000A<p>Facebook Platform product manager Mark Kinsey <a href="http://developers.facebook.com/news.php?blog=1&story=323">writes</a> on the Facebook Developers blog, "Today we're making the sharing experience on Facebook and off even richer by launching the next version of Facebook Share, with a live counter, as well as new ways to measure how content is being shared on Facebook."</p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16892&cb=16892" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16892&n=16892" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<p>While the cosmetic change is a nice feature for end users, the real news here is the analytics on the back end. Content creators and site owners can access the data associated with each shared item, including how often users share the link, how often they "like" shared content, how often they comment on the shared content on Facebook, and how often users click through from the shared item on Facebook to the original website.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>"You can do this programmatically by calling the links.getStats API method, or you can run an FQL query on the link_stat table," writes Kinsey. "By giving you access to this data for all URLs, we hope you'll create tools to help analyze and understand how users interact with your content on Facebook."</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The Facebook post further notes that <a href="http://techmeme.com">Techmeme</a>, <a href="http://bit.ly">bit.ly</a>, and <a href="http://awe.sm">awe.sm</a> have already put this data to use in analyzing traffic and monitoring user attention.</p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/facebook_launches_live_counts_for_sharing_widget.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/google_docs_logo_nov08.png" />With no fanfare or as much as an official announcement, Google has taken an important step in making users' Google Docs more open and portable.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>As of today, <a href="http://lifehacker.com/5389881/export-all-your-google-docs-to-a-zip-file">several</a> <a href="http://googlesystem.blogspot.com/2009/10/export-google-docs.html">bloggers</a> have reported seeing this new feature, which allows users to grab all their Google Docs and batch export them as a zip file. Files can be exported in a number of formats, including Microsoft Office and Open Office formats. Users can also choose to export only certain types of docs, e.g., spreadsheets and slide decks only.</p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16891&cb=16891" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16891&n=16891" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<p>The process is simple: Users select the documents they wish to export, click "More actions," then "Export."</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/googdocs1.jpg" /></p>\u000A\u000A<p>If a user is particularly pressed for time or has a larger chunk of data to export, he can also choose to navigate away and receive an email when the export is finished.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/googdocs2.jpg" /></p>\u000A\u000A<p>Unfortunately, any folders a user may have created or data related to authorship or shared documents do not seem to be included once documents are exported.</p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/all_your_docs_are_belong_to_you_google_docs_now_ex.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a VRetailers Try Twitter - Still Prefer Facebook, YouTube and MySpace
p484
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/Xk8q-Wkr5V8/internet_retailers_love_facebook_youtube_and_myspa.php

V<p><img alt="emarketer_logo_jul09.png" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/emarketer_logo_jul09.png" />Social networking sites are quickly becoming one of the most important places where retailers can meet potential customers and interact with their current customer base. According to a <a href="http://www.emarketer.com/Article.aspx?R=1007347">new report from eMarketer</a>, social network users are a lucrative target demographic because they are more likely to make online purchases than any other group. About three-quarters of all the retailers in the Internet Retailer <a href="http://www.internetretailer.com/top500guide/">Top 500 Guide</a> maintain a presence on at least one social network. Facebook, YouTube and MySpace are the most popular social networking sites for online retailers.</p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16890&cb=16890" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16890&n=16890" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Online Retailers Experiment with Twitter, But They Really Love Facebook's Platform</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>According to eMarkter's report, 56.8% of online retailers maintain a Facebook presence, 41.4% are on YouTube and 28.6% use MySpace. Twitter comes in at #4, as only 20.4% of all online merchants actively maintain a Twitter account. As eMarkteter points out, Twitter is a 'hotbed for experimentation,' where companies can promote deals and interact directly with their customers. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>For the majority of companies, however, Facebook is the most lucrative place to meet current and potential customers. Facebook's platforms give retailers ranging from 1-800-Flowers to Papa John's Pizza the ability to create <a href="http://www.marketingvox.com/1-800-flowers-pings-facebook-for-ecommerce-044752/">e-commerce applications</a> and provide users with services right on Facebook. </p>\u000A\u000A<p><img alt="emarketer_shopping_stats_oct09.png" align="right" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/emarketer_shopping_stats_oct09.png" />According to an earlier <a href="http://www.emarketer.com/Article.aspx?R=1007296">eMarkter report</a>, almost 99% of all US Online Retailers plan to have a Facebook fan site within the next year (up from 86% today), and 85% plan to use Twitter within the next 12 months.</p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Consumers Want Online Retailers to be on Social Networks</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>This trend, of course, isn't new, but it's also clear that online retailers will have to continue to follow their customers to where they are - and today, that means social networks like Twitter and Facebook. We also know that <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/majority_of_social_media_users_want_businesses_attention.php">consumers want to interact with brands</a> and online retailers through social networks, so any company that isn't using these tools is bound to miss out on potential sales. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>These customers are also highly likely to spread the word about a product - good or bad - on these social networks, so smart retailers will not just have a presence on these networks, but also use them to reach out directly to their customers. </p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/internet_retailers_love_facebook_youtube_and_myspa.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a />\u000A<a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/ERvOqvHIa8-68pyY1zqys0LtQII/1/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/ERvOqvHIa8-68pyY1zqys0LtQII/1/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=Xk8q-Wkr5V8:NecRBXMaBdw:FFnlKYwJmN0"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?d=FFnlKYwJmN0" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=Xk8q-Wkr5V8:NecRBXMaBdw:Ij26kaj3iuU"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?d=C2pbw5bZMiI" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=Xk8q-Wkr5V8:NecRBXMaBdw:yIl2AUoC8zA"><img VWhat are Hulu's Mysterious Plans?
p491
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/itQYd1Nftno/what_are_hulus_mysterious_plans.php
p492
sg7
(lp493
sg9
V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/hulu_logo_sep08.png" />Everyone is looking to <a href="http://www.hulu.com">Hulu</a> as the future of Internet TV. The joint venture between several major networks, Hulu delivers free, ad-supported programming via online streams - an untested model for long-term profitability, at least when it comes to television. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>While consumers have been enjoying the service since its launch in 2007, happily watching free TV shows and movies over their PCs and even their TV sets thanks to Media Center plugins and other <a href="http://www.macobserver.com/tmo/article/watching_hulu_and_much_more_on_your_apple_tv/">unofficial hacks</a>, the company itself is still trying to navigate this new online landscape and effectively monetize their content. Now recent statements by a News Corp exec have people wondering: can Hulu make the ad-supported model work? Or does the company have other plans? </p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16889&cb=16889" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16889&n=16889" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Is Hulu Working?</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>One of the primary objectives behind Hulu was to put free programming on the Internet to combat the rampant pirating of TV content that took place on sites like the popular file-sharing destination, The Pirate Bay. As iTunes did with music, the idea is to make using Hulu's service easier than having to go out and seek the illegal downloads. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Although iTunes charges for music on a per-file basis, Hulu, too has a business model that makes you pay - except in their case, you're paying with your eyeballs, not your credit card. Using video ads, Hulu has been attempting to monetize its service, but those efforts have been difficult at times. This spring, for instance, Screen Digest analyst Arash Amel claimed that Hulu had only sold about 60% of its ad inventory. "What we've seen is rapid growth in consumption, but the advertising isn't keeping up," <a href="http://newteevee.com/2009/03/31/analyst-hulu-to-bring-in-120-million-in-09/">he said</a>.</p> \u000A\u000A<p>While these figures, if accurate, could be reason for concern, many feel that the profitability of an online video venture of this nature takes time to develop. Eventually, the ad-supported model would work for Hulu as it has worked for numerous other websites and services, supporters claim. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Besides, more recent deals seem to bode well for the site. Case in point, this month the Publicis Groupe announced<a href="http://www.marketing-interactive.com/news/15525"> a mulit-million dollar ad deal </a>that involved targeted advertising to particular Hulu demographics. The deal is said to represent a "significant increase" in spending on Hulu. </p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Hulu to Charge?</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>Despite the promises ad deals like this hold, there is still debate as to whether or not Hulu is going to stick to the ad-supported model or try something new. At a conference last week, News Corp. deputy chairman Chase Carey made a pronouncement regarding this point that raised more than a few eyebrows:</p>\u000A\u000A<p>"I think a free model is a very difficult way to capture the value of our content. I think what we need to do is deliver that content to consumers in a way where they will appreciate the value,&quot; Carey <a href="http://www.broadcastingcable.com/blog/ADverse_Atkinson_on_Advertising/23941-Chase_Carey_Hulu_to_Charge_in_2010.php?nid=2228&source=title&rid=6454445">was quoted as saying by Broadcasting &amp; Cable</a>. "Hulu...needs to evolve to have a meaningful subscription model as part of its business."</p>\u000A\u000A<p>This seems to jibe with <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/hulu_to_add_subscription_services_pay-per-view.php">earlier reports</a> where News Corp. CEO Rupert Murdoch also hinted at the site's plans to add premium services by saying, "Are we looking at it with a view toward adding subscription services and pay per view? Yes we are." </p>\u000A\u000A<p>But "looking at" and "doing" are two very different things - where does Hulu stand now? Has their core philosophy - that is, their belief in the ad-supported model - changed? </p>\u000A\u000A<p>According to <a href="http://www.adweek.com/aw/content_display/news/digital/e3i62edbb41c75b175b959732a5437c873c"> AdWeek</a>, it has <u>not</u>. In the article, the company claims their ad-supported free service is still the one that "resonates with the largest group of users" and that any additional models would just serve to complement that.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>However, when we reached out to Hulu to ask about their plans regarding charging for content, the company wouldn't go on record with any such statement. </p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Why So Cagey? </h2>\u000A\u000A<p>Hulu's current decision to clam up could be taken in a few different ways. Perhaps they simply haven't decided what they're going to do about adding new premium services to Hulu and therefore don't want to discuss it <em>at all. </em></p>\u000A\u000A<p>Yet the quote they provided to AdWeek seems innocuous enough - so why not just stick with it? Why now choose to say nothing at all? Maybe they're hoping that with no quote, there is no story, and that will allow them to quell the impending panic among some users who are worried about Hulu's plans to make customers pay. Because some people are so opposed to paying for online content, just hearing reports that Hulu <em>might </em>change to a pay-to-stream model could dissuade them from continuing to use the service. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Then again, it could be that the opposite is true. Hulu wants to keep everyone wondering about what's coming next, generating excitement without providing any details. This means people can speculate wildly and give their opinions, allowing Hulu to tap into that online conversation about what people want before making any official decisions or announcements. </p>\u000A\u000A<h2>What We Think: Hulu Will Launch Value-Added Services</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>Despite any official confirmations from the company, we think it's pretty clear that Hulu has intentions to launch value-added services on top of its free, ad-supported model in the coming months. These may include pay-per-view options and some sort of subscription model. However, that subscription model would be there to provide users with value-added services that you couldn't get from the free model alone. Perhaps behind the scenes interviews? Sneak peeks? Actor interviews? Who knows...but the possibilities are endless. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>As to why we think that, it comes down to simple math. We've now seen three different statements about these premium services: Carey's recent remarks, Murdoch's quote from earlier this year, and <a href="http://blog.streamingmedia.com/the_business_of_online_vi/2009/10/sources-say-hulu-waiting-for-subscription-service-before-launching-iphone-app.html">anonymous sources quoted by Dan Rayburn</a> who hinted that Hulu's iPhone app won't launch until "Hulu rolls out a subscription based service." </p>\u000A\u000A<h2>...And They'll be Tied to the iPhone</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>The iPhone app, in fact, may be the real secret the company is trying to hide. Imagine if <a href="http://www.techmeme.com/090417/p64#a090417p64">the much-rumored and highly anticipated application</a> was linked to a subscription-based model. That could downright <em>revolutionize</em> the way people watch TV. Providing streaming content over the popular Apple smartphone would easily bring in additional revenue and that new source could quickly outperform the profits made by the ad-supported model. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Yet launching a Hulu iPhone app would be a challenge, as the company is undoubtedly aware. And, of course, Hulu wouldn't want to say anything about it, especially considering how difficult Apple is when it comes to applications that compete with their core services. Apple may not even approve such an application, claiming (rightly so) that it competes with iTunes. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>However, Apple may be loosening up on that front, with no small thanks going to the FCC <a href="http://www.businessinsider.com/did-apple-lie-about-rejecting-google-voice-iphone-app-2009-9">who recently questioned the company's rejection of the Google Voice application</a> - a VoIP dialer that Apple rejected because it competed with what the iPhone does natively. (Apple claims they're "still reviewing" it, but no one really buys that.) Since the FCC's involvement, however, Apple has gone on to <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/spotify_iphone_app_approved_thanks_to_the_fcc.php">approve a streaming music app called Spotify</a>, an application that many had feared would be rejected because it, even more so than Google Voice, competed with iTunes. That leaves us hopeful that a similar application launched by Hulu could also make it through the approval process. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Still, we wouldn't blame Hulu if they wanted to keep that extremely quiet. And that would certainly explain why Hulu won't comment on their plans. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Of course, this is all just speculation at this point, but we hope it turns out to be true.</p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/what_are_hulus_mysterious_plans.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/w7J8ttCpp9wdx6UxaoY5ak5Bolw/0/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/w7J8ttCpp9wdx6UxaoY5ak5Bolw/0/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a><br VFacebook Settlement Gets Judge's OK

Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/kwDgnJKA0r8/facebook_settlement_gets_judges_ok.php

V<em><strong><p>Proposal Would Kill Beacon, Have Facebook Paying $9.5 Million</p>\u000A</strong></em>\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/facebook_logo_feb09.png" />Late last week, a federal judge in California gave preliminary approval to a settlement of the class action lawsuit regarding Facebook's Beacon program. The controversial program, launched back in November of 2007, allowed Facebook users to share online purchases made on third-party affiliate websites with their social networking friends. The problem with the program was that it was opt-out instead of opt-in, angering many Facebook users who unknowingly shared information they wished they wouldn't have.</p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16888&cb=16888" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16888&n=16888" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A\u000A\u000A<p>One such victim was Sean Lane, now the lead plaintiff in the lawsuit. He was especially angry after the news of an Overstock.com purchase was posted to his Facebook profile. The purchase, a diamond ring he bought for his wife, was meant to be a surprise. After that incident, Lane, along with eighteen other plaintiffs, filed a class action lawsuit against Facebook, claiming that Beacon's opt-out option was "inadequate, misleading and deceptive." </p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Details of the Agreement: Shutting Down Beacon, Paying Damages, Non-Profit Foundation</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>The case has been in litigation since last year, but now looks like it's drawing to a close. U.S. District Court judge, Richard Seeborg in San Jose, has approved the proposed Facebook settlement that would have the company paying out $9.5 million, two-thirds of which would go to setting up a non-profit foundation to fund "projects and initiatives that promote the cause of online privacy, safety and security." The remaining money would then be split among the lawyers and the plaintiffs, each of whom would receive damages of $1000-15,000, according to <a href="http://www.mediapost.com/publications/?fa=Articles.showArticle&art_aid=116053">MediaPost</a>. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>The other major part to the Facebook settlement is the required termination of Facebook's Beacon program in its entirety. Although Facebook had quickly reacted to the Beacon outcry after its launch, <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/facebook_data_collection_update.php">changing the system over to opt-in</a> and even issuing <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/facebook_beacon_apology.php">a formal apology</a>, the program still exists today. (You can check your settings by going to Settings -&gt; Privacy Settings -&gt; Applications -&gt; Settings tab. Then scroll down to the bottom to see if "Beacon websites" is checked or unchecked. Checked will ensure no Beacon stories get posted to your profile).</p>\u000A\u000A<p>If the proposed settlement goes through, Facebook would then be relieved from liability from any future lawsuits regarding the same complaint and even those still pending like the <a href="http://www.mediapost.com/publications/?fa=Articles.showArticle&art_aid=80839">Facebook/Blockbuster class action suit</a> brought in April 2008.</p>\u000A\u000A<h2>Settlement Sounds Great...Especially for Facebook</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>On the surface, the proposed settlement sounds fair enough to all parties involved. Damages are paid and Facebook has to promote online privacy. However, as David Johnson points out on the <a href="http://www.digitalmedialawyerblog.com/2009/09/lane_v_facebook_privacy_class_1.html">Digital Media Lawyer Blog</a>, Facebook is <em>already </em>required by law to promote online privacy and the safety and security of its users' information per FTC mandates. In addition, Facebook would get to nominate one and have say over the other two board members on the proposed Privacy Foundation's board of directors. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Says Johnson: "Facebook effectively gets most of its money back to fund projects that it is already has an obligation to perform." </p>\u000A\u000A<p>Sounds like the real winner here may be Facebook. </p>\u000A\u000A<p><em>You can read the Settlement Agreement </em><a href="http://spamnotes.com/files/31236-29497/BeaconSettlement.pdf"><em>here</em></a><em>, courtesy of </em><a href="http://www.circleid.com/posts/a_look_at_the_facebook_privacy_class_action_beacon_settlement/"><em>CircleID</em></a><em>. The settlement was proposed last month, but only received preliminary approval on Friday. The affected parties have until February 1st to object to the proposed settlement.</em></p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/facebook_settlement_gets_judges_ok.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/RuOHbkc0ElK-LhNuq-Cw4sGDBBU/0/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/RuOHbkc0ElK-LhNuq-Cw4sGDBBU/0/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a><br />\u000A<a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/RuOHbkc0ElK-LhNuq-Cw4sGDBBU/1/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/RuOHbkc0ElK-LhNuq-Cw4sGDBBU/1/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=kwDgnJKA0r8:cCbhXVKQKmQ:FFnlKYwJmN0"><img VHow Moms Use Their iPhones
p505
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/ATClBOcKqjw/iphone_moms_shopping_entertaining_kids.php

V<p><img alt="greystripe_logo_oct09.png" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/greystripe_logo_oct09.png" />According to a new survey by mobile advertising network <a href="http://www.greystripe.com/">Greystripe</a>, mothers with iPhones regularly let their children use their phones, download games specifically for their children and often use their phones at grocery stores to compare prices and check their grocery lists.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Not too long ago, mothers were still considered to be a hard group to reach through mobile applications because they tend to be late adopters. The iPhone's mainstream success has changed this, however, and iPhone moms have now become a desirable target demographic for marketers.</p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16885&cb=16885" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16885&n=16885" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<div><a name="fb_share" type="box_count" href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php">Share</a></div>\u000A<p>Greystripe is a brand-focused advertising network and obviously has an interest in making this group attractive for advertisers, but the statistics in this report seem pretty solid. Greystripe found the 1,294 respondents who filled out this survey through house ads on its own network. </p>\u000A\u000A<p></p>\u000A\u000A<h2>The iPhone Mom</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>According to Greystripe, 96% of mothers with iPhones are involved in their family's purchasing decisions and 40% are the sole decision makers. Eighty percent have attended at least some college and are slightly more likely to have received a Graduate degree than the rest of the iPhone user base. The age of the children in these families skews slightly older, with 29% of the moms having children between 0 and 4, while 43% have children between 15 and 17.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img alt="iphone_moms_stats.png" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/iphone_moms_stats.png" /></p>\u000A\u000A<h2>How iPhone Moms Use Their Phones: Shopping and Keeping the Kids Entertained</h2>\u000A\u000A<p>What is more interesting, though, is how these moms use their iPhones. Fifty-nine percent of all iPhone moms let their children use their phones and 41% download games specifically for their children. Twenty percent also download educational content for their kids. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>With regards to shopping, 79% of all iPhone moms use their phones for 'shopping related activities.' The majority of these activities consist of locating stores (60%). Thirty-nine percent also use the phone to compare prices. Nineteen percent of iPhone moms download coupons, 23% look for items on sale and 37% use their phones to learn about products. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>When it comes to using the phone in stores, 42% of the mothers who responded to the Greystripe survey said that they regularly use their phones at the grocery store. Grocery list applications - or just the Notes app on the iPhone and iPod touch - are the most popular uses for the iPhone and 19% of all moms use these. Thirteen percent of moms also use the phone to look up prices in the store itself - which explains the popularity of apps like <a href="http://www.redlaser.com/">Red Laser</a>.</p>\u000A\u000A<p><img alt="greystripe_moms_stats_2.png" src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/greystripe_moms_stats_2.png" /></p>\u000A\u000A<p>As Greystripe's founder and CEO Michael Chang told us last week, this data shows how the iPhone has become a tool for everyday life for this demographic. This group tends to have a large influence over everyday purchase decisions in their families and these iPhone moms often use their phones to make a good number of these decisions, which make them an attractive target for marketers.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>This study also shows that there is a large market for apps that are specifically geared towards this demographic, including mobile price comparison apps or apps that can deliver mobile coupons - and a lot of iPhone dads will probably be interested in these apps as well.</p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/iphone_moms_shopping_entertaining_kids.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/VZ_u14MW9TOlQl2c2iWMQ0dSRIY/0/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/VZ_u14MW9TOlQl2c2iWMQ0dSRIY/0/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a><br />\u000A<a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/VZ_u14MW9TOlQl2c2iWMQ0dSRIY/1/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/VZ_u14MW9TOlQl2c2iWMQ0dSRIY/1/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a></p><div class="feedflare">\u000A<a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=ATClBOcKqjw:2VrbtYhaAPQ:FFnlKYwJmN0"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?d=FFnlKYwJmN0" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=ATClBOcKqjw:2VrbtYhaAPQ:Ij26kaj3iuU"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?d=Ij26kaj3iuU" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=ATClBOcKqjw:2VrbtYhaAPQ:C2pbw5bZMiI"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?d=C2pbw5bZMiI" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=ATClBOcKqjw:2VrbtYhaAPQ:yIl2AUoC8zA"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?d=yIl2AUoC8zA" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=ATClBOcKqjw:2VrbtYhaAPQ:V_sGLiPBpWU"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?i=ATClBOcKqjw:2VrbtYhaAPQ:V_sGLiPBpWU" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=ATClBOcKqjw:2VrbtYhaAPQ:gIN9vFwOqvQ"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?i=ATClBOcKqjw:2VrbtYhaAPQ:gIN9vFwOqvQ" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=ATClBOcKqjw:2VrbtYhaAPQ:F7zBnMyn0Lo"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?i=ATClBOcKqjw:2VrbtYhaAPQ:F7zBnMyn0Lo" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?a=ATClBOcKqjw:2VrbtYhaAPQ:OqabYuBsmOY"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/readwriteweb?d=OqabYuBsmOY" border="0" VIBM Debuts Food Traceability iPhone App
p512
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/readwriteweb/~3/X9j17HWcxWI/ibm_debuts_food_traceability_iphone_app.php
p513

(lp514

V<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/breadcrumbs_150.jpg" />Today at the <a href="http://www.ibm.com/software/data/conf/">IBM Information on Demand</a> event, IBM will demo a new app that will bring the Internet of Things to the iPhone. The as yet unreleased iPhone app is called <strong>Breadcrumbs</strong> and it will give consumers access to information about grocery food items. The app will be able to scan barcodes and deliver a summary of the ingredients in a food item, along with when it was manufactured. That data is usually on the food label, but Breadcrumbs goes a step further - it can provide extra information such as product recall data. If a product has been recalled in the past, this app will tell the consumer all of the relevant details.</p>\u000A<p align="right"><em>Sponsor</em><br /><a href="http://d1.openx.org/ck.php?n=16887&cb=16887" target="_blank"><img src="http://d1.openx.org/avw.php?zoneid=11205&cb=16887&n=16887" border="0" alt="" align="right" /></a></p>\u000A\u000A<p><img src="http://www.readwriteweb.com/images/ibm_breadcrumbs.jpg" align="right" />Breadcrumbs is able to scan barcodes using the iPhone's camera. The consumer simply points their iPhone at a food item and gets back relevant data. Other than product recall details, the information returned to the user is mostly the same as what's on food labels - only it is pulled from the Web. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>IBM told ReadWriteWeb that when 4G becomes common place in mobile phones, then apps such as Breadcrumbs will become more powerful and be readily used on-the-fly by consumers when grocery shopping.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The larger trend here is <strong>the convergence of smart phones with the <a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/top_5_web_trends_of_2009_internet_of_things.php">Internet of Things</a></strong> (i.e. Internet-connected real world objects). Devices such as the iPhone essentially become sensor and RFID readers, which allow consumers to interact with real world objects in a much more detailed manner.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>Breadcrumbs is a glimpse of what we'll see in the near future, when information will literally - <em>finally</em> - be at the consumer's fingertips when they're shopping for groceries or any other goods where data is plentiful. Up till now, data such as product recall information has largely been inaccessible to consumers - at least when at the grocery store. </p>\u000A\u000A<p>In the long term expect to see apps like Breadcrumbs provide data on where and when food items get consumed, together with how long they were on the shelf before being consumed. Apps like Breadcrumbs may even be able to tell <em>who</em> consumed the items (privacy advocates, start your engines!). These apps will also be useful in determining counterfeit items, for example when buying an expensive luxury good.</p>\u000A\u000A<p>The date that Breadcrumbs will be launched on iPhone has not yet been announced by IBM.</p>\u000A<strong><a href="http://www.readwriteweb.com/archives/ibm_debuts_food_traceability_iphone_app.php#comments-open">Discuss</a></strong>\u000A<p><a href="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/bk3iW2dvcLHVj-4Kb0ErrU8ud8E/0/da"><img src="http://feedads.g.doubleclick.net/~at/bk3iW2dvcLHVj-4Kb0ErrU8ud8E/0/di" border="0" ismap="true" /></a><br VLooking At Platforms
p519
sg5
Vhttp://feedproxy.google.com/~r/Diversitynetnz/~3/yGThdxv3vso/

(lp521
sg9
V<p>Earlier this year at the Enterprise 2.0 conference \u201Cplatform\u201D was the name of choice. Seemingly every company I spoke to was a platform player. It seems the latest \u201Cfart on demand\u201D <a rel="nofollow" class="zem_slink" title="iPhone" href="http://www.apple.com/iphone">iPhone</a> application is a \u201Cplatform for virtual flatulence generation\u201D, that the latest <a rel="nofollow" class="zem_slink" title="Twitter" href="http://twitter.com/">Twitter</a> clone with negligible uptake is \u201Ca platform for global collaboration\u201D and the maker of a time tracking widget is \u201Ca platform for enterprise efficiency and ROI generation\u201D \u2013 I can\u2019t help but rail against that and yell \u201Cenough of the platform already!\u201D</p>\u000A<p>One of the sessions at the conference included half a dozen or so vendors of microblogging products, true they all had various takes on the theme and offered different services, but they shared the common feature of providing microblogging. Somewhat surprisingly every one of them proclaimed that they were a platform. I couldn\u2019t help but ask a somewhat tongue-in-cheek question \u2013 when every single product on the web calls itself a platform, we\u2019ll have to invent a new word to let wannabe players impress VCs.</p>\u000A<p>The inimitable Phil Wainewright recently released an excellent <span><a rel="nofollow" href="http://ippblog.intuit.com/blog/2009/10/redefining-software-platforms---how-paas-changes-the-game-for-isvs.html">report</a></span> looking at different aspects of PaaS, I thought I'd try and bring a&nbsp;philosophical&nbsp;bent to the&nbsp;discussion.</p>\u000A<p>In my mind, to claim the moniker \u201Cplatform\u201D a service needs to have a number of attributes; an ecosystem, critical mass, beachhead status and openness. So what different types of platforms do I see out there?</p>\u000A<p><strong>Monotheistic platforms</strong></p>\u000A<p>What I\u2019ve playfully called monotheistic platforms leverage one particular business process and attempt to build a platform around that. It\u2019ll always be a niche but so long as it\u2019s a big enough niche it\u2019s worth following. <a rel="nofollow" class="zem_slink" title="Force.com" href="http://force.com/">Force.com</a> is the originator of the <a rel="nofollow" class="zem_slink" title="Platform as a service" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Platform_as_a_service">PaaS</a> moniker. It\u2019s clearly gaining an ecosystem, with third parties developing applications that live within its world and it\u2019s also seemingly gaining some critical mass. Force.com however is less than open \u2013 it dictates how applications can be written, it dictates (to a certain extent) how applications look and it\u2019s central view of the world is CRM-centric (although admittedly less so now than even a few months ago). Force.com is a platform but it\u2019s what I\u2019ll call a niche platform.</p>\u000A<p><strong>Like Switzerland, only different, and bigger</strong></p>\u000A<p>Platforms that span the divide between on-premises and SaaS and that do so in a neutral way are arguably something of a nirvana. These platforms interact seamlessly with the web environment, while also federating to on-premises applications. They also broaden the offering such that vendors can chose parts of the stack to adopt (billing, authentication, data models etc). As for size, like anything in business, reach is critical and this is where the incumbent players have an edge \u2013 having the ability to leverage an existing customer based but introduce them to a platform is the gold many platform plays would die for. I\u2019ve <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.google.com/cse?cx=008057045071378771690:c-gaqnbeaks&ie=UTF-8&q=ipp&sa=Search">written</a> before about the <span><a rel="nofollow" href="https://ipp.developer.intuit.com/">Intuit Partner Platform</a></span> (<em>disclosure \u2013 IPP is a client</em>) and I contend that it\u2019s an exemplar of this type of platform play \u2013 both from a vendor perspective and an end-user centric viewpoint.</p>\u000A<p><strong>Ego Platforms \u2013 The Id</strong></p>\u000A<p>To use <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Id,_ego,_and_super-ego">Freud\u2019s term</a>, these platforms cater for the Id part of our personalities \u2013 these social platforms are built around individuals core desire to connect and find meaning from the people around them \u2013 exhibit one, <a rel="nofollow" class="zem_slink" title="Facebook" href="http://facebook.com/">Facebook</a>. One can\u2019t deny that Facebook has true critical mass, it also has a plethora of third parties creating offerings surrounding it. It\u2019s beachhead proposition is \u201Cthe social graph\u201D but again it\u2019s fairly closed. I\u2019d temper that last statement however to say that <a rel="nofollow" class="zem_slink" title="Facebook Connect" href="http://developers.facebook.com/connect.php">Facebook Connect</a> is a move towards becoming a more open, amorphous platform.</p>\u000A<p><strong>Pantheism</strong></p>\u000A<p>Pantheism is the view that everything is part of an all-encompassing, immanent God. Without talking about the utility or otherwise of Twitter, it is the ultimate pantheistic example. To continue the pantheistic analogy, it is a platform that doesn\u2019t focus at all on the anthromorphic expression of itself, rather it\u2019s an abstract expression \u2013 the \u201Ctweet\u201D is a semi-abstract thing that takes on different shapes and forms at different times. The ecosystem that has built up around Twitter is phenomenal \u2013 this is precisely because it\u2019s a platform that doesn\u2019t dictate where players are or how they look. From this point of view Twitter is ultimately open. The critical mass they have is a little debatable looking at statistics of users who are actual active. Twitter\u2019s beachhead status is communication \u2013 often vacuous communication it must be admitted but communication nonetheless.</p>\u000A<p><strong>Co-operation</strong></p>\u000A<p>Co-operative platforms attempt to build critical mass through symbiosis. <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.thesmallbusinessweb.com/">The Small Business Web</a> is a good example of this. The Small Business Web, according to its founding partners</p>\u000A<blockquote><p>is a movement to bring together like-minded, customer-obsessed software companies to integrate our respective products and make life easier for small businesses. While there are many products available for small business owners on the Web, the approach we're taking is to use each others APIs to provide a high-level of integration between these applications and create a more seamless experience for our customers.</p>\u000A</blockquote>\u000A<p>In other words a bunch of small SaaS start-ups got together to try and build an alternative to the single site best-of-breed application. By working together on integrations, they\u2019re slowly build the ability for small businesses to pick and mix functionality according to their specific needs.</p>\u000A<p><strong>Summary</strong></p>\u000A<p>Not eveyone can be a platform, but everyone sure wants to be. I\u2019d be keen to hear readers thoughts about this post and how they see the platform battles shaking down over the next year or two.</p>\u000A</p>\u000A</p>\u000A</p>\u000A</p>\u000A</p>\u000A</p>\u000A<div class="zemanta-pixie"><img class="zemanta-pixie-img" alt="" src="http://img.zemanta.com/pixy.gif?x-id=ca115cd6-3023-43ec-b886-34617f302ce2" /></div>\u000A<div align="right"><font size="1" color="#868686">CloudAve is exclusively sponsored by </font><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.zoho.com"><img src="http://www.cloudave.com/images/zoho.png" align="absmiddle" border="0px" /></a></div>\u000A<div class="feedflare">\u000A<a rel="nofollow" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/CloudAve?a=vQ5YqkZYwDg:m8OHrlCp_KY:YwkR-u9nhCs"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/CloudAve?d=YwkR-u9nhCs" border="0" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/CloudAve?a=vQ5YqkZYwDg:m8OHrlCp_KY:V_sGLiPBpWU"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/CloudAve?i=vQ5YqkZYwDg:m8OHrlCp_KY:V_sGLiPBpWU" border="0" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/CloudAve?a=vQ5YqkZYwDg:m8OHrlCp_KY:gIN9vFwOqvQ"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/CloudAve?i=vQ5YqkZYwDg:m8OHrlCp_KY:gIN9vFwOqvQ" border="0" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/CloudAve?a=vQ5YqkZYwDg:m8OHrlCp_KY:qj6IDK7rITs"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/CloudAve?d=qj6IDK7rITs" border="0" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/CloudAve?a=vQ5YqkZYwDg:m8OHrlCp_KY:3QFJfmc7Om4"><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/CloudAve?i=vQ5YqkZYwDg:m8OHrlCp_KY:3QFJfmc7Om4" border="0" /></a>\u000A</div>\u000A<p><img src="http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/CloudAve/~4/vQ5YqkZYwDg" height="1" width="1" /></p>

VUnemployment does get boring
p528
sg5
Vhttp://www.geekzone.co.nz/Jama/6897

(lp530

VI have been a techno recluse for the last few months and I know that a few of you might have been wondering where I disappeared to. Well, I can tell you now that I have been through a very frustrating time. <br /><br />In July I was made redundant from my very short lived role of Brand Manager at Renaissance Brands. I don't consider myself a vicitim but more of a casualty of the current economic climate. I was employed to bring on the 'next big thing', an investment for the future; unfortunately I quickly became an expensive liability. The digital Freeview PVR was going to be the hero product but the TVNZ TiVo announcement gave Renaissance management cold feet so the project was dumped. We had actually signed an agreement with Magic TV which I thought was an excellent product regardless of TiVo. It is good see that freeviewshop has picked up the product.<br /><br />Fortunately money has not been an issue for us, well not yet anyway. But we have had to change our lifestyle slightly. For the first 2 months of unemployment I worked on our house during what was apparently the worst Wellington Winter in 30 years and I managed to paint the house inside and out. Quite a feat when you consider that we hang off a hill and the scaffolding was 30 meters high! I even painted the roof which is probably one of the scariest things I have done. All the work paid off as we sold our house in 7 days and at a good price. In the next 4 weeks we are dramactically downsizing. Moving from our modern, 3 storey house in central Wellington with the hell harbour view to a little 2 bedroom old house in the Hutt hills. Fortunately we have this option, the house in the Hutt is our rental property which we have owned for a number of years but it will be a shock to the system none the less.<br /><br />I have seriously lost count of how many jobs I have applied for; sometimes your application is acknowledged, sometimes not. Sometimes you get to meet with a recruitment consultant and sometimes you get an interview with the employer. All very frustrating and how the market has changed. Probably 2 years ago it was a job hunters&nbsp;market, loads of jobs and too few&nbsp;applicants and now it is exactly the opposite. It is a lengthy process as well; one position I applied for dragged on for 8 weeks from initial application to interview to not being successful and I really, really liked the role.<br /><br />After 20 odd years working at the cutting edge of technology in a variety of roles I have started to consider other options and have been looking at purchasing an exisiting business. It is possible that to secure a financial future for my family I may have to buy myself a job. Not necessarily where I want to be but I know my wife has probably had enough of me being at home. On the positive side though I have been able to spend lots of time with my 4 year old son and we are good mates. I know he doesn't want me to go back to work.<br /><br /><br />
